<h4><span class="mw-headline" id=".22Siege.22">"Siege"</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Siege_(comics)" title="Siege (comics)">Siege (comics)</a></div>
<p>In the "<a href="/wiki/Siege_(comics)" title="Siege (comics)">Siege</a>" storyline, Tony Stark is seen under the care of <a href="/wiki/Thor_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Thor (Marvel Comics)">Dr. Donald Blake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maria_Hill" title="Maria Hill">Maria Hill</a>. When the two spot the attack on Asgard, Blake tells Maria to run away with Stark.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Hill leaves Stark to assist Blake, now as <a href="/wiki/Thor_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Thor (Marvel Comics)">Thor</a>, after his ambush by <a href="/wiki/Green_Goblin" title="Green Goblin">Osborn</a> and his attack dog the <a href="/wiki/Sentry_(Robert_Reynolds)" title="Sentry (Robert Reynolds)">Sentry</a>. Hill rescues Thor and brings him back to Broxton to recuperate. When Osborn declares <a href="/wiki/Martial_law" title="Martial law">martial law</a> and unleashes <a href="/wiki/Daken" title="Daken">Daken</a> and the Sentry on Broxton to root out Thor and Hill, Thor reveals himself to defend the town. Hill returns to Tony Stark's hiding place to move him to a safer location and are joined soon after by <a href="/wiki/Speed_(comics)" title="Speed (comics)">Speed</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Young_Avengers" title="Young Avengers">Young Avengers</a>, who holds a certain <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man%27s_armor" title="Iron Man's armor">indestructible suitcase</a> that Edwin Jarvis had given Captain America earlier. Hill orders Speed to surrender when Stark stops her and asks Speed to give him the case. While Osborn is battling the <a href="/wiki/The_New_Avengers_(comics)" title="The New Avengers (comics)">New Avengers</a>, Stark appears in a variant of his MK III armor and proceeds to disable Osborn's Iron Patriot armor. Osborn orders the Sentry to annihilate Asgard, rather than allow the Avengers to have it, which the Sentry does, practically leveling the city before the horrified eyes of Thor. After Asgard falls, literally, Stark stands alongside his fellow heroes, as the now armor-free Osborn exclaims they are all doomed and he 'was saving them from him' pointing up towards a <a href="/wiki/Sentry_(Robert_Reynolds)#Void" title="Sentry (Robert Reynolds)">Void</a>-possessed Sentry hovering over them.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> As the Void tears apart the teams, Loki gives them the power to fight back through the <a href="/wiki/Norn_Stones" title="Norn Stones">Norn Stones</a>. When the Void kills Loki, Thor's rage-fueled blows rattle the creature. Tony then tells Thor to get the Void away from Asgard, which he does. Tony then drops the commandeered H.A.M.M.E.R. Helicarrier 'as a bullet', subduing the Void. When Robert Reynolds begs to be killed, Thor denies the request, but is forced to when the Void resurfaces. Sometime later, the Super-Human Registration Act is repealed and Tony is given back his company and armory. As a symbol for their heroics and their new unity, Thor places a remaining Asgardian tower on Stark Tower where the Watchtower once stood.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id=".22Heroic_Age.22">"Heroic Age"</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Heroic_Age_(comics)" title="Heroic Age (comics)">Heroic Age (comics)</a></div>
<p>In the 2010-2011 "Stark: Resilient" storyline, Tony builds a new armor, the Bleeding Edge, with the help of Mister Fantastic. This new armor fully utilizes the repulsor tech battery embedded in his chest to power Tony's entire body and mind thus allowing him access to extremis once more. Furthermore, the battery operates as his "heart" and is predominantly the only thing keeping him alive.<sup id="cite_ref-Fraction.2C_Matt_2010_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fraction.2C_Matt_2010-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> Later, Tony announces that he will form a new company, Stark Resilient. He states that he will stop developing weapons, instead, he plans to use his repulsor technology to give free energy to the world. Justine and Sasha Hammer create their own armored hero, Detroit Steel, to take Stark's place as the Army's leading weapons-builder. Stark's plan consists of building two repulsor-powered cars. The Hammers try to foil his efforts. The first car is destroyed by sabotage, while Detroit Steel attacks Stark Resilient's facilities while Tony tests the second car. Through a legal maneuver, Tony is able to get the Hammers to stop their attacks and releases a successful commercial about his new car.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id=".22Fear_Itself.22">"Fear Itself"</span></h4>
<p>In the 2011 "<a href="/wiki/Fear_Itself_(comics)" title="Fear Itself (comics)">Fear Itself</a>" storyline, Earth is attacked by the Serpent, brother of Odin.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> In Paris, Iron Man fights <a href="/wiki/Grey_Gargoyle" title="Grey Gargoyle">Grey Gargoyle</a>, who has become Mokk, Breaker of Faith and one of the Serpent's Worthy. Mokk leaves Iron Man unconscious and transforms Detroit Steel into stone. When Iron Man awakens, he sees that Mokk has turned all the people in Paris into stone and left.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> To defeat the Serpent's army, Tony drinks a bottle of wine - thus 'sacrificing' his sobriety - to gain an audience with Odin, who allows Tony to enter the realm of Svartalfheim. There, Tony and the dwarves of Svartalfheim work to build weapons the Avengers can use against the Worthy.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Tony upgrades his armor with uru-infused enchantments and delivers the finished weapons to the Avengers, who use them for the final battle against the Serpent's forces. Iron Man watches as Thor kills the Serpent, but dies in the process. After the battle is over, Tony melts down the weapons he created and repairs Captain America's shield, which had been broken by Serpent, and gives it back to Captain America, telling him that the shield is now stronger.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> During a subsequent argument with Odin about the gods' lack of involvement in the recent crisis, Odin gives Tony a brief opportunity to see the vastness of the universe the way he sees it, before, as thanks for Tony's role in the recent crisis, he restores all the people that the Grey Gargoyle killed during his rampage.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_of_the_Mandarin_and_Marvel_NOW.21">Return of the Mandarin and Marvel NOW!</span></h4>
<p>In the storylines "Demon" and "The Long Way Down", Stark is subpoenaed by the U.S. government after evidence surfaces of him using the Iron Man armor while under the influence of intoxicants. Mandarin and Zeke Stane upgrade some of Iron Man's old enemies and send them to commit acts of terrorism across the world, intending to discredit Iron Man. General Bruce Babbage forces Stark to wear a tech governor, a device that allows Babbage to deactivate Stark's armor whenever he wants. To fight back, Tony undergoes a surgical procedure that expels the Bleeding Edge technology out of his body and replaces his repulsor node with a new model, forcing Babbage to remove the tech governor off his chest. He announces his retirement as Iron Man, faking Rhodes' death and giving him a new armor so that he becomes the new Iron Man.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> This leads into the next storyline, "The Future", in which the Mandarin takes control of Stark's mind and uses him to create new armored bodies for the alien spirits inhabiting his rings, but Stark allies himself with some of his old enemies, who have also been imprisoned by Mandarin, and manages to defeat and escape him. The final issue of this storyline concluded Matt Fraction's series.<sup id="cite_ref-IronMan523_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IronMan523-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the ongoing series that premiered in 2012 as part of the <a href="/wiki/Marvel_NOW!" title="Marvel NOW!">Marvel NOW!</a> relaunch, Tony Stark has hit a technological ceiling. After the death of Dr. Maya Hansen and the destruction of all of the Extremis Ver. 2 kits that were being sold to the black market, Tony decides that the Earth is not safe without him learning more from what's in the final frontier. He takes his new suit, enhanced with an artificial intelligence named P.E.P.P.E.R. and joins <a href="/wiki/Peter_Quill" title="Peter Quill" class="mw-redirect">Peter Quill</a> and The <a href="/wiki/Guardians_of_the_Galaxy_(2008_team)" title="Guardians of the Galaxy (2008 team)">Guardians of the Galaxy</a> after helping them thwart a Badoon attack on Earth.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Powers_and_abilities">Powers and abilities</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armor">Armor</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man%27s_armor" title="Iron Man's armor">Iron Man's armor</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IronManV5No25.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/63/IronManV5No25.jpg/350px-IronManV5No25.jpg" width="350" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/63/IronManV5No25.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/63/IronManV5No25.jpg 2x" data-file-width="495" data-file-height="213" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IronManV5No25.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Bleeding Edge Armor, like the Extremis Armor before it, is stored in Stark's bones, and can be assembled and controlled by his thoughts.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Iron Man possesses <a href="/wiki/Powered_exoskeleton" title="Powered exoskeleton">powered armor</a> that gives him superhuman strength and durability, flight, and an array of weapons. The armor is invented and worn by Stark (with occasional short-term exceptions). Other people who have assumed the Iron Man identity include Stark's long-time partner and best friend <a href="/wiki/War_Machine" title="War Machine">James Rhodes</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-DeFalco211_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeFalco211-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> close associates <a href="/wiki/Happy_Hogan" title="Happy Hogan">Harold "Happy" Hogan</a>; Eddie March;<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> and (briefly) <a href="/wiki/Guardsman_(Michael_O%27Brien)" title="Guardsman (Michael O'Brien)" class="mw-redirect">Michael O'Brien</a>.</p>
<p>The weapons systems of the suit have changed over the years, but Iron Man's standard offensive weapons have always been the repulsor rays that are fired from the palms of his <a href="/wiki/Gauntlet_(glove)" title="Gauntlet (glove)">gauntlets</a>. Other weapons built into various incarnations of the armor include: the uni-beam projector in its chest; pulse bolts (that pick up <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">kinetic energy</a> along the way; so the farther they travel, the harder they hit); an <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_pulse" title="Electromagnetic pulse">electromagnetic pulse</a> generator; and a defensive energy shield that can be extended up to 360 degrees. Other capabilities include: generating ultra-<a href="/wiki/Freon" title="Freon">freon</a> (i.e., a freeze-beam); creating and manipulating <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_field" title="Magnetic field">magnetic fields</a>; emitting sonic blasts; and projecting 3-dimensional <a href="/wiki/Hologram" title="Hologram" class="mw-redirect">holograms</a> (to create decoys).</p>
<p>In addition to the general-purpose model he wears, Stark has developed several specialized <a href="/wiki/Space_suit" title="Space suit">suits</a> for <a href="/wiki/Spaceflight" title="Spaceflight">space travel</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-IronMan142_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IronMan142-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_diving_suit" title="Atmospheric diving suit">deep-sea diving</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stealth_technology" title="Stealth technology">stealth</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-DeFalco202_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeFalco202-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IronMan152_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IronMan152-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> and other special purposes. Stark has modified suits, like the Hulkbuster heavy armor. The Hulkbuster armor is composed of add-ons to his so-called modular armor, designed to enhance its strength and durability enough to engage the Incredible <a href="/wiki/Hulk_(comics)" title="Hulk (comics)">Hulk</a> in a fight. A later model, designed for use against <a href="/wiki/Thor_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Thor (Marvel Comics)">Thor</a>, is modeled on the <a href="/wiki/Destroyer_(Thor)" title="Destroyer (Thor)">Destroyer</a> and uses a mystical power source. Stark develops an electronics pack during the Armor Wars that, when attached to armors that use Stark technologies, will burn out those components, rendering the suit useless. This pack is ineffective on later models. While it is typically associated with <a href="/wiki/War_Machine" title="War Machine">James Rhodes</a>, the War Machine armor began as one of Stark's specialty armors.</p>
<p>The most recent models of Stark's armor, beginning with the Extremis Armor, are now stored in the hollow portions of Stark's bones, and the personal area networking implement used to control it is implanted in his forearm, and connected directly to his <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a>.</p>
<p>The Extremis has since been removed,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific volume in which the source appears. (April 2014)">volume&#160;&amp;&#160;issue&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and he now uses more conventional armors. Some armors still take a liquid form but are not stored within his body.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Powers">Powers</span></h3>
<p>After being critically injured during a battle with the Extremis-enhanced Mallen, Stark injects his nervous system with modified techno-organic virus-like body restructuring machines (the Extremis process).<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> By rewriting his own biology, Stark is able to save his life, gain an enhanced <a href="/wiki/Healing_factor" title="Healing factor">healing factor</a>, and partially merge with the Iron Man armor, superseding the need for bulky, AI-controlled armors in favor of lighter designs, technopathically controlled by his own brain. His enhanced technopathy extends to every piece of technology, limitless and effortlessly due to his ability to interface with communication satellites and wireless connections to increase his "range". Some components of the armor-sheath are now stored in Tony's body, able to be recalled, and extruded from his own skin, at will.</p>
<p>During the "<a href="/wiki/Secret_Invasion" title="Secret Invasion">Secret Invasion</a>" storyline the Extremis package is catastrophically shutdown by a virus, forcing him again to rely on the previous iteration of his armor, and restoring his previous limitations. Furthermore, Osborn's takeover of most of the few remaining Starktech factories, with Ezekiel Stane systematically crippling the others, limits Tony to the use of lesser, older and weaker armors.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After being forced to "wipe out" his brain to prevent Norman Osborn from gaining his information, Tony Stark is forced to have a new arc reactor, of <a href="/wiki/Iron_Fist_(comics)" title="Iron Fist (comics)">Rand</a> design installed in his chest. The process greatly improves his strength, stamina and intellect. The procedure left him with virtually no autonomic functions: as his brain was stripped of every biological function, Tony is forced to rely on a digital backup of his memories (leaving him with severe gaps and lapses in his long-term memory) and on software routine in the arc reactor for basic stimuli reaction, such as blinking and breathing.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>Bleeding Edge</i> package of armor and physical enhancement is now equal in power, if not a more advanced, version of the old Extremis tech.<sup id="cite_ref-Fraction.2C_Matt_2010_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fraction.2C_Matt_2010-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Skills">Skills</span></h3>
<p>Tony Stark is an inventive genius whose expertise in the fields of <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a> rivals that of <a href="/wiki/Mister_Fantastic" title="Mister Fantastic">Reed Richards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hank_Pym" title="Hank Pym">Hank Pym</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hulk_(comics)" title="Hulk (comics)">Bruce Banner</a>, and his expertise in <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineering" title="Mechanical engineering">mechanical engineering</a> surpasses even theirs. He is regarded as one of the most intelligent characters in the Marvel Universe. He graduated with advanced degrees in physics and engineering at the age of 17 from <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a> (MIT)<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> and further developed his knowledge ranging from <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> to <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum mechanics</a> as time progressed. His expertise extends to his ingenuity in dealing with difficult situations, such as difficult foes and deathtraps, in which he is capable of using available tools, including his suit, in unorthodox but effective ways. He is well respected in the business world, able to command people's attention when he speaks on economic matters, having over the years built up several multi-million dollar companies from virtually nothing. He is noted for the loyalty he commands from and returns to those who work for him, as well as for his business ethics. Thus he immediately fired an employee who made profitable, but illegal, sales to <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Doom" title="Doctor Doom">Doctor Doom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IronMan149_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IronMan149-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> He strives to be environmentally responsible in his businesses.</p>
<p>At a time when Stark was unable to use his armor for a period, he received some combat training from <a href="/wiki/Captain_America" title="Captain America">Captain America</a> and has become physically formidable on his own when the situation demands it.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, Stark possesses great business and political acumen. On multiple occasions he reacquired control of his companies after losing them amid corporate takeovers.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Due to his membership in the Illuminati, Iron Man was given the Space <a href="/wiki/Infinity_Gem" title="Infinity Gem" class="mw-redirect">Infinity Gem</a> to safeguard.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> It allows the user to exist in any location (or all locations), move any object anywhere throughout the universe and warp or rearrange space. As with the other members of the lluminati and their respective gems, Iron Man has vowed not to use it on any occasion, even after the Secret Invasion and his fugitive status.</p>
<p>It was suggested that Stark's intelligence was the result of experiments made by a <a href="/wiki/Recorder_(comics)" title="Recorder (comics)" class="mw-redirect">Rigellian recorder</a> called <a href="/wiki/Recorder_451" title="Recorder 451">Recorder 451</a> after his mother almost loses him while pregnant, in exchange of saving his life.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> However, it was revealed that Tony was really adopted and the true son of Howard and Maria Stark is <a href="/wiki/Arno_Stark" title="Arno Stark" class="mw-redirect">Arno</a>, weakened by 451's experiments.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_versions">Other versions</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alternative_versions_of_Iron_Man" title="Alternative versions of Iron Man">Alternative versions of Iron Man</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_other_media">In other media</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_in_other_media" title="Iron Man in other media">Iron Man in other media</a></div>
<p>In 1966, Iron Man was featured in a series of cartoons.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1981, Iron Man guest appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_and_His_Amazing_Friends" title="Spider-Man and His Amazing Friends">Spider-Man and His Amazing Friends</a></i>, but only as Tony Stark.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> He went on to feature again in his own series in the 1990s as part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Marvel_Action_Hour" title="Marvel Action Hour" class="mw-redirect">Marvel Action Hour</a></i> with the Fantastic Four; <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hays" title="Robert Hays">Robert Hays</a> provided his voice in these animated cartoons. Iron Man makes an appearance in the episode "Shell Games" of <i><a href="/wiki/Fantastic_Four:_World%27s_Greatest_Heroes" title="Fantastic Four: World's Greatest Heroes">Fantastic Four: World's Greatest Heroes</a>.</i> Apart from comic books, Iron Man appears in Capcom's <i>"Vs."</i> video games, including <i><a href="/wiki/Marvel_Super_Heroes_(arcade_game)" title="Marvel Super Heroes (arcade game)" class="mw-redirect">Marvel Super Heroes</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Marvel_vs._Capcom:_Clash_of_Super_Heroes" title="Marvel vs. Capcom: Clash of Super Heroes">Marvel vs. Capcom: Clash of Super Heroes</a></i> as either a Gold War Machine or Hyper Armor War Machine, <i><a href="/wiki/Marvel_vs._Capcom_2:_New_Age_of_Heroes" title="Marvel vs. Capcom 2: New Age of Heroes">Marvel vs. Capcom 2: New Age of Heroes</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Marvel_vs._Capcom_3:_Fate_of_Two_Worlds" title="Marvel vs. Capcom 3: Fate of Two Worlds">Marvel vs. Capcom 3: Fate of Two Worlds</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Marvel_vs._Capcom_3" title="Ultimate Marvel vs. Capcom 3">Ultimate Marvel vs. Capcom 3</a></i>. Iron Man is a playable character in <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_(video_game)" title="Iron Man (video game)">Iron Man</a></i>, the 1992 arcade game <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_America_and_the_Avengers" title="Captain America and the Avengers" class="mw-redirect">Captain America and the Avengers</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Marvel:_Ultimate_Alliance" title="Marvel: Ultimate Alliance">Marvel: Ultimate Alliance</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Marvel:_Ultimate_Alliance_2" title="Marvel: Ultimate Alliance 2">its sequel</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Marvel_Nemesis:_Rise_of_the_Imperfects" title="Marvel Nemesis: Rise of the Imperfects">Marvel Nemesis: Rise of the Imperfects</a></i>, as well as being featured as an unlockable character in <i><a href="/wiki/X-Men_Legends_II:_Rise_of_Apocalypse" title="X-Men Legends II: Rise of Apocalypse">X-Men Legends II: Rise of Apocalypse</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Tony_Hawk%27s_Underground" title="Tony Hawk's Underground">Tony Hawk's Underground</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2009 animated series, <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man:_Armored_Adventures" title="Iron Man: Armored Adventures">Iron Man: Armored Adventures</a></i>, most of the characters, including Tony Stark, are teenagers. An <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Anime" title="Marvel Anime">anime adaptation</a> began airing in Japan in October 2010 as part of a collaboration between <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Animation" title="Marvel Animation">Marvel Animation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madhouse_(company)" title="Madhouse (company)">Madhouse</a>, in which Stark, voiced by <a href="/wiki/Keiji_Fujiwara" title="Keiji Fujiwara">Keiji Fujiwara</a>, travels to Japan where he ends up facing off against the Zodiac.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, a film adaptation titled <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_(2008_film)" title="Iron Man (2008 film)">Iron Man</a></i> was released, starring <a href="/wiki/Robert_Downey,_Jr." title="Robert Downey, Jr.">Robert Downey, Jr.</a> as Tony Stark and directed by <a href="/wiki/Jon_Favreau" title="Jon Favreau">Jon Favreau</a>. <i>Iron Man</i> received very positive reviews from film critics,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> grossing $318 million domestically and $585 million worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-boxmojo_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boxmojo-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Its video game adaptation met generally negative reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> The character of Tony Stark, again played by Robert Downey, Jr., appeared at the end of the 2008 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Incredible_Hulk_(film)" title="The Incredible Hulk (film)">The Incredible Hulk</a></i>. Downey reprised his role in <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_2" title="Iron Man 2">Iron Man 2</a></i> (2010), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">Marvel's The Avengers</a></i> (2012), and <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_3" title="Iron Man 3">Iron Man 3</a></i> (2013), and will appear in <i><a href="/wiki/Avengers:_Age_of_Ultron" title="Avengers: Age of Ultron">Avengers: Age of Ultron</a></i> (2015), and a third <i>Avengers</i> film (TBA).<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_influence">Cultural influence</span></h2>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Rapping" title="Rapping">rapper</a> <a href="/wiki/Ghostface_Killah" title="Ghostface Killah">Ghostface Killah</a>, a member of <a href="/wiki/Wu-Tang_Clan" title="Wu-Tang Clan">Wu-Tang Clan</a>, titled his 1996 debut solo album <i><a href="/wiki/Ironman_(Ghostface_Killah_album)" title="Ironman (Ghostface Killah album)">Ironman</a></i>, and has since continued to use lyrics related to the Iron Man comics and <a href="/wiki/Sampling_(music)" title="Sampling (music)">samples</a> from the animated TV shows on his records.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shaheem_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shaheem-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> He has adopted the nickname Tony Starks as one of his numerous alter-egos<sup id="cite_ref-Shaheem_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shaheem-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> and was featured in a scene deleted from the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_(2008_film)" title="Iron Man (2008 film)"><i>Iron Man</i> film</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Magneto_and_Titanium_Man" title="Magneto and Titanium Man">Magneto and Titanium Man</a>" was inspired by the <a href="/wiki/X-Men" title="X-Men">X-Men</a>'s nemesis and the original version of the Iron Man villain. Another Iron Man villain, the Crimson Dynamo, is mentioned in the lyrics to this song.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>The British band <a href="/wiki/Razorlight" title="Razorlight">Razorlight</a> mentions Tony Stark in a verse of their song, "Hang By, Hang By".<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>The character of <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Stark" title="Nathan Stark" class="mw-redirect">Nathan Stark</a> on the television show <i><a href="/wiki/Eureka_(U.S._TV_series)" title="Eureka (U.S. TV series)">Eureka</a></i> is inspired by Tony Stark.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> has ranked Iron Man among the wealthiest fictional characters on their annual ranking,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> while <i><a href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" title="BusinessWeek" class="mw-redirect">BusinessWeek</a></i> has ranked him as one of the ten most intelligent characters in American comics.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2011, <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> ranked Iron Man 12th in the Top 100 Comic Book Heroes.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Two Iron Man-themed trucks compete in the <a href="/wiki/Monster_Jam" title="Monster Jam">Monster Jam</a> monster truck racing series. Debuted in Atlanta on 9 January 2010, they are driven by Lee O' Donnell and Morgan Kane.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>

<div id="powerbox-holder">
<div id="powerbox">
<div id="pbox_hdr">&nbsp;</div>
<p><b>Universe</b><br /><a href="/universe/Marvel_Universe" title="Marvel Universe">Marvel Universe</a>
</p><p>
<b>Real Name</b><br />Anthony Edward "Tony" Stark
</p><p>
<b>Aliases</b><br />"Shellhead," "Golden Avenger," "Tetsujin"; formerly Crimson Dynamo, Iron Knight, Hogan Potts, "Spare Parts Man"; impersonated Cobalt Man (Ralph Roberts)
</p><p>
<b>Identity</b><br />Publicly Known
</p><p>
<b>Citizenship</b><br />U.S.A.
</p><p>
<b>Place of Birth</b><br />Long Island, New York
</p><p>
<b>First Appearance</b><br />Tales of Suspense #39 (1963)
</p><p>
<b>Origin</b><br />Tales of Suspense #39 (1963) 
</p><div class="myLink" id="char-sigissues">Significant Issues<div id="char-sigissues-content" class="togCont" style="display: none;">Red and gold armor debuted (Tales of Suspense #48, 1963); traveled to Camelot with Dr. Doom (Iron Man #149-150, 1981); succumbed to alcoholism (Iron Man #167-182, 1983-1984); Jim Rhodes became Iron Man (Iron Man #169-199, 1983-1985); Tony Stark returned as Iron Man in red &amp; silver armor (Iron Man #200, 1985); fought <a href="/universe/Armor_Wars" title="Armor Wars">Armor Wars</a> against armored villains (Iron Man #225-231, 1987-1988); traveled to Camelot again with Doom (Iron Man #249-250, 1989); manipulated by Kearson DeWitt in "Armor Wars II" (Iron Man #258-266, 1990 -1991); James Rhodes took over as Iron Man (Iron Man #284, 1992); Tony Stark became Iron Man again (Iron Man #289, 1993); helped form Force Works (Force Works #1, 1994); time traveled with Dr. Doom (Iron Man #11, 1997); returned from Counter-Earth (Iron Man #1, 1998); revealed as member of Hell Fire Club (X-Men #73, 1998); armor became sentient, killed Whiplash (Iron Man #26-30, 2000); Ultron took control of armor (Iron Man #46-49, 2001-2002); became Secretary of Defense (Iron Man #73-78, 2003); infiltrated the Thunderbolts as Cobalt Man (Avengers/Thunderbolts #1-6, 2004); helped form new group of Avengers (New Avengers #1, 2005); became Director of S.H.I.E.L.D. (Civil War #7, 2007)</div></div><div class="myLink" id="char-occupation">Occupation<div id="char-occupation-content" class="togCont" style="display: none;">Adventurer, president emeritus of Stark Industries, founder of Maria Stark Foundation; formerly director of S.H.I.E.L.D., CEO of Stark Industries, Stark Solutions, Stark Enterprises, Circuits Maximus &amp; Stark International, US Secretary of Defense, computer technician</div></div><div class="myLink" id="char-relatives">Known Relatives<div id="char-relatives-content" class="togCont" style="display: none;"><a href="/universe/Stark,_Howard" title="Stark, Howard">Howard Anthony Stark</a> (father, deceased), <a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=Stark,_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stark, Maria (page does not exist)">Maria Collins Carbonell Stark</a> (mother, deceased), <a href="/universe/Stark,_Morgan" title="Stark, Morgan">Morgan Stark</a> (cousin), <a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=Stark,_Edward&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stark, Edward (page does not exist)">Edward Stark</a> (uncle, deceased), <a href="/universe/Stark,_Sr.,_Isaac" title="Stark, Sr., Isaac">Isaac Stark, Sr.</a>, <a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=Stark,_Jr.,_Isaac&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stark, Jr., Isaac (page does not exist)">Isaac Stark, Jr.</a> (ancestors, deceased)</div></div><div class="myLink" id="char-affiliation">Group Affiliation<div id="char-affiliation-content" class="togCont" style="display: none;">Formerly <a href="/universe/Avengers" title="Avengers">Avengers</a>, <a href="/universe/Initiative" title="Initiative">Initiative</a>, <a href="/universe/Hellfire_Club" title="Hellfire Club">Hellfire Club</a> (outer circle), <a href="/universe/S.H.I.E.L.D." title="S.H.I.E.L.D.">S.H.I.E.L.D.</a>, <a href="/universe/Illuminati" title="Illuminati">Illuminati</a>, <a href="/universe/Thunderbolts" title="Thunderbolts">Thunderbolts</a>, <a href="/universe/Force_Works" title="Force Works">Force Works</a>, <a href="/universe/Queen%27s_Vengeance" title="Queen&#39;s Vengeance">Queen's Vengeance</a>, Alcoholics Anonymous</div></div><div class="myLink" id="char-education">Education<div id="char-education-content" class="togCont" style="display: none;">Ph.D.s in physics and electrical engineering</div></div><div class="myLink" id="char-physicals">Physical Attributes<div id="char-physicals-content" class="togCont" style="display: none;">
<p><b>Height</b><br />6'1"; (in armor) 6'6"
</p><p>
<b>Weight</b><br />225 lbs.; (in armor) 425 lbs.
</p><p>
<b>Eyes</b><br />Blue
</p><p>
<b>Hair</b><br />Black
</p></div></div><div class="myLink" id="char-powers">Powers<div id="char-powers-content" class="togCont" style="display:none;">None; Tony's body had been enhanced by the modified techno-organic virus, Extremis, but it is currently inaccessible and inoperable.</div></div><div class="myLink" id="char-abilities">Abilities<div id="char-abilities-content" class="togCont" style="display:none;">Tony has a genius level intellect that allows him to invent a wide range of sophisticated devices, specializing in advanced weapons and armor. He possesses a keen business mind.</div></div><div class="myLink" id="char-weapons">Weapons<div id="char-weapons-content" class="togCont" style="display:none;">The Iron Man armor includes Tony’s primary energy weapon, repulsor rays, a powerful particle beam which is standard equipment in the palms of his armor; the repulsor ray can repel physical and energy-based attacks, traveling as either a single stream or as a wide-field dispersal. The armor has also been outfitted with pulse bolts (extremely powerful plasma discharges which grow in strength as they seek their target), sonic generators, explosive shell projectiles, mini-missiles, magnetic field generators and a laser torch built into the finger of Tony’s gauntlet. The armor’s surface can generate an electric charge to dispel attackers.</div></div><div class="myLink" id="char-paraphernalia">Paraphernalia<div id="char-paraphernalia-content" class="togCont" style="display:none;">Tony’s most recent armor is protected by an energy-draining shield which expands from the gauntlets, as well as a personal deflector shield. The armor grants Tony superhuman strength (lifting 100 tons at maximum power). Its Jet boots enable flight at Mach 8; he can also hover utilizing a localized gravity field. The armor’s internal air supply lasts more than one hour and can be sealed for travel through low oxygen, underwater or outer space environments. The armor also features a chronometer, radar, sonar, a magnometer, an atom-force microscope, photon, heat, motion and other sensor instruments. The armor contains a subspace/satellite radio communications array which receives local radio and video signals; the armor can also jam transmissions. The chest plate features the unibeam, a powerful searchlight that can project beams in virtually every light spectrum (visible, infrared and ultraviolet); it also features a laser beam projector, an EMP (electromagnetic pulse) generator which can shut down electronic devices within a 50-yard radius, a scanning device that travels along energy waves emitted from the unibeam and a holographic generator.</div></div><div id="connections_lnk"><a href="http://marvel.com/universe3zx/utility/network.htm?character_id=2619" class="external text" title="http://marvel.com/universe3zx/utility/network.htm?character_id=2619" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Launch Connections</a></div></div></div>
<div id="headshot"><a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=File:IronMan_Head.jpg&amp;filetimestamp=20090911174114" class="image" title="IronMan Head.jpg"><img alt="" src="http://i.annihil.us/u/prod/marvel//universe3zx/images/thumb/f/f5/IronMan_Head.jpg/406px-IronMan_Head.jpg" width="406" height="321" border="0" /></a>
</div>
<p><br />
</p>
<div id="bio_wrapper">
<div id="biobody">A "cool exec with a heart of steel," Tony Stark is the invincible Iron Man, fighting for justice as a modern day knight in high-tech armor.
<p><br />
</p>

<a name="Before_the_Iron_Mask" id="Before_the_Iron_Mask"></a><h2> <span class="mw-headline"> Before the Iron Mask </span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:125px;"><a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=File:TonyStark.jpg&amp;filetimestamp=20100416173903" class="image" title="TonyStark.jpg"><img alt="" src="http://i.annihil.us/u/prod/marvel//universe3zx/images/2/26/TonyStark.jpg" width="123" height="351" border="0" class="thumbimage" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"></div></div></div>Anthony "Tony" Stark was born to <a href="/universe/Stark,_Howard" title="Stark, Howard">Howard Anthony Stark</a> and <a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=Stark,_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stark, Maria (page does not exist)">Maria Collins Carbonell Stark</a>, owners of the prominent US firm, Stark Industries. As a boy, Tony was fascinated with building and controlling machines. At the age of 15 Tony entered the undergraduate electrical engineering program at the Massachusetts Institute of Technology (MIT), and graduated with two master’s degrees by age 19. Tony went to work for Stark Industries, but showed more interest in living a reckless playboy lifestyle than using his engineering skills. At the age of 21, Tony inherited <a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=Stark_Enterprises&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stark Enterprises (page does not exist)">Stark Enterprises</a> when his parents were killed in a car accident secretly orchestrated by rival corporation Republic Oil (later ROXXON). Still lacking in business acumen, Tony promoted secretary Virginia "Pepper" Potts to be his executive assistant and left the majority of his workload on her so that he could avoid what he saw as a burden.
<p><br />
</p>
<a name="A_Self-Made_Superhero" id="A_Self-Made_Superhero"></a><h2> <span class="mw-headline"> A Self-Made Superhero </span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=File:ManyArmors.jpg&amp;filetimestamp=20080121200043" class="image" title="The Many Armors of Iron Man"><img alt="" src="http://i.annihil.us/u/prod/marvel//universe3zx/images/thumb/9/9d/ManyArmors.jpg/180px-ManyArmors.jpg" width="180" height="216" border="0" class="thumbimage" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=File:ManyArmors.jpg&amp;filetimestamp=20080121200043" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/universe3zx/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="Enlarge Image" title="Enlarge Image" border="0" /></a></div>The Many Armors of Iron Man</div></div></div> Tony personally attended a field test of his military hardware at one of his international plants; however, soon after his arrival Stark’s party was attacked by a gang of terrorists led by the Sin-Cong revolutionary <a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=Chu,_Wong&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chu, Wong (page does not exist)">Wong Chu</a>. During the skirmish, a land mine went off and lodged a piece of shrapnel near Tony’s heart. Taken back to Wong-Chu’s camp, Tony shared a cell with Professor Ho Yinsen, a world-famous physicist. Wong-Chu demanded that the two scientists develop advanced weaponry for his forces. Knowing that he could not live long with the shrapnel so close to his heart, Tony proposed that he and Yinsen devote their gifts to creating one of the battlesuits he had been developing, equipped with a magnetic field generator to prevent the shrapnel from reaching his heart. The armor they created became the first true Iron Man armor and was equipped with crude magnetic weaponry for defense. While the armor’s battery was being powered, some of Wong-Chu’s men attempted to break in on the proceedings. Yinsen went to create a diversion and was shot to death by Wong-Chu’s men. When the battery had finished charging, Tony went into battle as Iron Man and tore Wong-Chu’s camp apart. He eventually returned to the USA with the aid of US Marine <a href="/universe/Rhodes,_James" title="Rhodes, James" class="mw-redirect">James "Rhodey" Rhodes</a>. Tony offered Rhodey a job with his company should he ever need one.
<p>At first, Tony found his new life a torment; his armor’s chest plate had to be worn constantly and required frequent recharging. He kept the armor a secret from everyone, including his fiancée, Joanna Nivena. Turning suicidal and drinking heavily, Tony was supported by Joanna, with whom he shared his secret identity. Joanna encouraged him to use his armor as a super hero, but ultimately called off the engagement knowing Tony would not be the family man she desired.
</p><p>Tony worked to improve the Iron Man armor and claimed Iron Man was Tony Stark's personal bodyguard to disguise his identity. Tony played a dual-role with the formation of the<a href="/universe/Avengers" title="Avengers">Avengers</a> both as the sponsor and, as Iron Man, as a founding member along with <a href="/universe/Thor_(Thor_Odinson)" title="Thor (Thor Odinson)">Thor</a>, <a href="/universe/Yellowjacket_(Henry_Pym)" title="Yellowjacket (Henry Pym)" class="mw-redirect">Ant-Man (Henry Pym)</a>, the <a href="/universe/Wasp" title="Wasp">Wasp (Janet van Dyne)</a>, and the <a href="/universe/Hulk_(Bruce_Banner)" title="Hulk (Bruce Banner)">Hulk</a>. While pursuing <a href="/universe/Namor" title="Namor" class="mw-redirect">Namor the Sub-Mariner</a>, Iron Man came across the comatose body of <a href="/universe/Captain_America" title="Captain America" class="mw-redirect">Captain America (Steve Rogers)</a> Rogers), the famous World War II super hero, preserved on ice. Revived, Captain America joined the Avengers and became an important teammate and friend to Tony. Later, Tony helped establish the international super-spy agency <a href="/universe/SHIELD" title="SHIELD" class="mw-redirect">SHIELD</a> to combat terrorist threats.
</p><p>During these early years as a super hero, Iron Man battled <a href="/universe/Mandarin" title="Mandarin">Mandarin</a>, <a href="/universe/Hawkeye_(Clint_Barton)" title="Hawkeye (Clint Barton)">Hawkeye</a>, and the <a href="/universe/Black_Widow_(Natasha_Romanova)" title="Black Widow (Natasha Romanova)">Black Widow(Natasha Romanova)</a>. 
</p><p><br />
</p>
<a name="A_Change_of_Heart" id="A_Change_of_Heart"></a><h2> <span class="mw-headline"> A Change of Heart</span></h2>
<p>Tony found himself drawn to the beautiful Whitney Frost, but she proved to be the daughter of the Avengers’ foe Count Nefaria and a high-ranking member of the Maggia crime syndicate. Seeking to steal Tony’s inventions, she pitted agents such as <a href="/universe/Whiplash_(Mark_Scarlotti)" title="Whiplash (Mark Scarlotti)"> Whiplash (Mark Scarlotti)</a> and <a href="/universe/Gladiator_(Melvin_Potter)" title="Gladiator (Melvin Potter)"> Gladiator (Melvin Potter)</a> against him. After using one of his Life Model Decoys (LMDs) to deceive the Mandarin and protect his identity, Tony was horrified when the LMD developed an independent personality and usurped his identity. The LMD, believing itself superior to Tony, obtained a suit of Iron Man armor and began running Stark Industries while the real Tony was away. Unable to prove his identity, Tony fell into the clutches of Madame Masque (a newly garbed Whitney Frost), agent of the gold-loving Mordecai Midas, who attempted to force Stark to turn over his fortune. Tony used his original Iron Man armor to destroy the LMD imposter, but suffered another heart attack in the process. The Avengers rushed him to a hospital where Dr. Jose Santini transplanted a synthetic heart into his chest so that Tony no longer required his chest plate to live.
</p><p>Following the Avengers’ involvement in the interstellar Kree-Skrull War, Iron Man joined <a href="/universe/Mister_Fantastic" title="Mister Fantastic">Mr. Fantastic</a>, <a href="/universe/Black_Bolt" title="Black Bolt">Black Bolt</a> of the <a href="/universe/Inhumans" title="Inhumans">Inhumans</a>, <a href="/universe/Professor_X" title="Professor X">Professor Xavier</a> of the <a href="/universe/X-Men" title="X-Men">X-Men</a>, sorcerer <a href="/universe/Doctor_Strange_(Stephen_Strange)" title="Doctor Strange (Stephen Strange)">Dr. Stephen Strange</a> and Namor in founding the <a href="/universe/Illuminati" title="Illuminati">Illuminati</a>, a secret organization designed to share knowledge and pool resources against major threats.
</p><p><br />
</p>
<a name="Hero_of_Iron.2C_Feet_of_Clay" id="Hero_of_Iron.2C_Feet_of_Clay"></a><h2> <span class="mw-headline"> Hero of Iron, Feet of Clay</span></h2>
<p>Renaming his corporation Stark International, Tony resolved to abandon munitions production in favor of electronics and computer engineering after witnessing firsthand the impact his company’s weapons had on innocent lives. 
</p><p>Despite seeming to have everything a man could want, Tony was under much stress. The machinations of rival industrialist Justin Hammer and SHIELD’s constant pressure drove Tony further into drinking. His girlfriend at the time, Bethany Kabe, kept Tony from continued succumbing to his alcoholism. Their relationship ended when Bethany’s presumed-dead husband was discovered alive.
</p><p>In opposing <a href="/universe/Iron_Monger" title="Iron Monger">Obidiah Stane's</a> attempts at forming a major multinational conglomerate, Tony unwittingly made Stane a driven enemy. Obadiah Stane set up games of psychological warfare against Tony, which included physical attacks by his Chessmen super-operatives, outbidding Stark International for key contracts and having his lackey Indries Moomji romance Tony, all in an attempt to drive Tony to resort to drinking. As Stane’s pressure increased, Tony responded as anticipated, and after Indries rejected Tony, he virtually gave up trying to oppose Stane. When the villain Magma (Jonathan Darque) attacked Stark International, Tony proved too drunk to wage a competent battle and instead revealed his double identity to Rhodes. With Tony passed out, Rhodes donned the armor and defeated Magma. Tony told Rhodes to keep the armor and turned his back on Stark International while he proceeded to drink himself out of his company, property and fortune until all of his assets were frozen. Obadiah Stane stepped in and claimed Stark International, renaming it Stane International, but Rhodes prevented Stane from obtaining the Iron Man armors.
</p><p>Tony had hit rock-bottom, homeless and perpetually drunk. However, helping deliver a baby put life into perspective and he began his path of recovery and sobriety joining Alcoholics Anonymous.
</p><p>Tony, James, and James’ friends, Morley and Clytemnestra Erwin set up a California-based new corporation: <a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=Circuits_Maximus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Circuits Maximus (page does not exist)">Circuits Maximus</a>. Obadiah planted a bomb in their laboratory, killing Morley and badly injuring Rhodes. Tony constructed his most advanced armor yet at the new West Coast Avengers Compound and confronted Stane, who had designed his own armored identity as the Iron Monger. When Tony defeated the Iron Monger, Stane committed suicide.
</p><p><br />
</p>
<a name="Armor_Wars" id="Armor_Wars"></a><h2> <span class="mw-headline"> Armor Wars</span></h2>
<p>After joining the West Coast Avengers, Iron Man provided sanctuary from reformed villain Force (Clay Wilson), an agent of Justin Hammer. Examining Force’s armor, Tony recognized familiar circuitry patterns based on his own Iron Man armor designs. Tony discovered that his old foe <a href="/universe/Spymaster" title="Spymaster" class="mw-redirect">Spymaster</a> had stolen his designs and sold them to Hammer who armored several of his super villain clients, including the Beetle (Abner Jenkins), the Controller, the Mauler (Brendan Doyle), the Raiders and Stilt-Man (Wilbur Day). Enraged by the thought that innocent people might have been killed with his technology, Tony resolved to eliminate all traces of his technology that had fallen into outside hands. However, Iron Man falsely accused federal agent Stingray of possessing Stark’s technology, forcing Tony to publicly fire his alter-ego. Steve Rogers was stripped of his Captain America identity, and became the Captain; Tony supplied him with a force shield. Unable to trust anyone using his armor technology, Tony targeted the Guardsmen at the Vault prison. The Captain tried to stop Iron Man, severely straining their friendship. Iron Man next attacked the Crimson Dynamo in Russia, and accidentally killed the Titanium Man, leading to Iron Man’s expulsion from the Avengers. Tony faked Iron Man’s death, and later rejoined the Avengers as the “new Iron Man.” Eventually, the Avengers saw through Tony’s facade.
</p>
<a name="Start_of_the_Breakdown" id="Start_of_the_Breakdown"></a><h2> <span class="mw-headline">Start of the Breakdown</span></h2>
<p>After being shot and paralyzed by former love interest Kathleen Dare, Tony installed a biochip into his body to regain mobility. The biochip gained the attention of corporate foe Kearson DeWitt, who held grievances against Tony. DeWitt hijacked the biochip and took control of Tony’s nervous system. Though Tony regained control of his body using his armor, but by the time he had defeated DeWitt his body was so damaged he could barely move. Tony donned a skintight neuronet suit to help him function, but his armor became the only certain way to keep himself alive. After defeating the Mandarin, and using a rogue team of Avengers to seemingly destroy the Supreme Intelligence (against Avengers’ leader Captain America’s command), he expressed his regret to Captain America and the two began trying to repair their fractured relationship. As Tony’s health continued to deteriorate, he designed his variable threat assessment armor (model 11, also called the “War Machine”) and won back Stane International’s assets from its last owner, Justin Hammer. Succumbing to total nervous system failure, Tony seemingly died on an operating table. In his will, he made Rhodes the new CEO of Stark Enterprises and left the War Machine armor for him to carry on as Iron Man. Rhodes respected his wishes.
</p><p><br />
</p>
<a name="A_New_Beginning" id="A_New_Beginning"></a><h2> <span class="mw-headline">A New Beginning</span></h2>
<p>Tony was secretly in cryogenic storage while his body’s entire nervous system was essentially rebuilt. Revived, Tony had to undergo intense physical therapy. Rhodes, who was infuriated at being deceived, immediately quit Stark Enterprises. Tony allowed Rhodes to keep the War Machine armor and launched a new model of armor, the Neuromimetic Telepresence Unit 150 (NTU-150),which he could control remotely while he recovered. He also used artificial intelligences to aid him in his work, including HOMER and PLATO.
</p><p>Outfitted in his new modular armor, Tony agreed to end the West Coast Avengers, but formed <a href="/universe/Force_Works" title="Force Works">Force Works</a>. Providing his team with full access to his cutting edge technology. 
</p><p><br />
</p>
<a name="Teen_Tony" id="Teen_Tony"></a><h2> <span class="mw-headline"> Teen Tony</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=File:Ironman02.jpg&amp;filetimestamp=20070611212932" class="image" title="Iron Man with the Avengers"><img alt="" src="http://i.annihil.us/u/prod/marvel//universe3zx/images/thumb/3/3e/Ironman02.jpg/200px-Ironman02.jpg" width="200" height="300" border="0" class="thumbimage" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=File:Ironman02.jpg&amp;filetimestamp=20070611212932" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/universe3zx/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="Enlarge Image" title="Enlarge Image" border="0" /></a></div>Iron Man with the Avengers</div></div></div>Some time later the villain <a href="/universe/Immortus" title="Immortus">Immortus</a>, posing as his alternate reality version of himself <a href="/universe/Kang" title="Kang">Kang the Conqueror</a>, took control of Tony Stark as a sleeper agent. Tony was forced to kill <a href="/universe/Yellowjacket_(Rita_DeMara)" title="Yellowjacket (Rita DeMara)">Yellowjacket</a> (Rita DeMara) and <a href="/universe/Crystal" title="Crystal">Crystal</a>'s Nanny, Marilla. To battle the combined forces of Iron Man and “Kang,” the Avengers were forced to recruit an alternate reality’s <a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=Iron_Man_(Timeslide)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Iron Man (Timeslide) (page does not exist)">teenage version</a> of Tony Stark from Earth-96020. Teen Tony stole a suit of armor from Stark International and aided the Avengers in battle. When the adult version came face to face with his teenage self he was finally able to overcome Immortus' control. Tony sacrificed himself to save the younger Tony’s life and defeated Immortus.
<p>Teenage Tony Stark continued to fight with the Avengers and took control of Stark International. The mutant <a href="/universe/Onslaught_(entity)" title="Onslaught (entity)">Onslaught</a> manifested, threatening life on Earth. The young Tony and many of the world's super heroes fought Onslaught in New York City's Central Park where young Iron Man, the <a href="/universe/Fantastic_Four" title="Fantastic Four">Fantastic Four</a>, Thor, the Hulk, and other heroes seemingly lost their lives defending the <a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Earth (page does not exist)">Earth</a>. However, they were actually brought into a <a href="/universe/Counter-Earth_(Franklin_Richards)" title="Counter-Earth (Franklin Richards)">pocket universe</a> created by <a href="/universe/Mister_Fantastic" title="Mister Fantastic">Reed</a> and <a href="/universe/Invisible_Woman" title="Invisible Woman">Sue Richards</a>' son, <a href="/universe/Richards,_Franklin" title="Richards, Franklin">Franklin</a>. Events soon forced Franklin to choose a world to survive; he restored the original world. Upon returning, the still-adult Tony found he had the collective memories and experiences of the original Tony Stark merged with those of the Earth-96020 Tony and the person he had been on Counter-Earth.
</p><p><br />
</p>
<a name="Secrets_and_Lies" id="Secrets_and_Lies"></a><h2> <span class="mw-headline"> Secrets and Lies </span></h2>
<p>When Iron Man defeated the villain Mentallo, Tony took advantage of the situation and used Mentallo’s global mind control device to erase all knowledge of his often-compromised secret identity from every person on Earth. He then revealed it to those people he deemed trustworthy, causing them to remember the memories he had buried.
</p><p>Former Avenger <a href="/universe/Jocasta" title="Jocasta">Jocasta</a>, a creation of the villainous robot <a href="/universe/Ultron" title="Ultron">Ultron</a>, was forced to prepare the Iron Man armor to become Ultron’s new home; the process accelerated when Iron Man was hit by a lightning bolt, causing Tony to suffer a heart attack at the same time. Thinking that the armor had been granted its own consciousness, Tony attempted to teach the armor; the benign Ultron-12 aspect of its personality was receptive, but the cruelty of most past Ultron models corrupted the armor and it murdered <a href="/universe/Whiplash_(Mark_Scarlotti)" title="Whiplash (Mark Scarlotti)">Whiplash</a> during a fight. However, the armor ultimately sacrificed its “life” to save Tony, whose heart was failing. After implanting a robotic “heart” in Tony’s chest that saved him, the armor deactivated.
</p><p>Tony later decided to reveal his secret identity to the world, and was offered work as a contractor for the US Department of Defense. Though turning down that opportunity, he accepted the post as the President's Secretary of Defense to monitor the use of his technology by the United States military. Tony’s tenure as Secretary of Defense ended in scandal when the insane <a href="/universe/Scarlet_Witch_(Wanda_Maximoff)" title="Scarlet Witch (Wanda Maximoff)">Scarlet Witch</a> caused him to engage in drunken and belligerent behavior at the United Nations. Disgraced, Tony was quickly drummed out of his position. The Scarlet Witch’s growing insanity led to the dissolution of the Avengers when her out-of-control powers wrecked Avengers Mansion and killed several teammates. Tony was further smeared when one-time corporate rival Clarence Ward stole Iron Man armor, using it to kill the Stark Industries board and Rumiko, Tony’s girlfriend. Iron Man defeated Ward and recalled all of the Iron Man armors he had granted to the military. He then publicly “resigned” as Iron Man but secretly intended to continue operating, again claiming it was another man wearing the armor.
</p><p><br />
</p>
<a name="Extremis" id="Extremis"></a><h2> <span class="mw-headline"> Extremis </span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=File:Ironman-extremis.jpg&amp;filetimestamp=20100416170553" class="image" title="Ironman-extremis.jpg"><img alt="" src="http://i.annihil.us/u/prod/marvel//universe3zx/images/thumb/6/67/Ironman-extremis.jpg/100px-Ironman-extremis.jpg" width="100" height="137" border="0" class="thumbimage" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=File:Ironman-extremis.jpg&amp;filetimestamp=20100416170553" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/universe3zx/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="Enlarge Image" title="Enlarge Image" border="0" /></a></div></div></div></div> Iron Man clashed with Mallen, a terrorist enhanced by the Extremis virus, a techno-organic agent designed by Tony’s one-time classmate Maya Hansen and intentionally leaked so that the world could see its destructive potential. Mallen defeated Iron Man, nearly mortally wounding Tony in the process. Tony had Maya inject him with the Extremis, gambling on it saving his life and increasing his strength so that he could face Mallen as an equal. The process resulted in Tony’s body rebuilding itself with superior organs and he found that he could now link to virtually any computer on Earth; the newly enhanced Tony killed Mallen in a rematch.
<p><br />
</p>
<a name="Civil_War" id="Civil_War"></a><h2> <span class="mw-headline"> Civil War </span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=File:Ironman01.jpg&amp;filetimestamp=20070611213035" class="image" title="Captain America fighting Iron Man"><img alt="" src="http://i.annihil.us/u/prod/marvel//universe3zx/images/thumb/f/f0/Ironman01.jpg/200px-Ironman01.jpg" width="200" height="133" border="0" class="thumbimage" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=File:Ironman01.jpg&amp;filetimestamp=20070611213035" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/universe3zx/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="Enlarge Image" title="Enlarge Image" border="0" /></a></div>Captain America fighting Iron Man</div></div></div> During a televised raid of a house containing escaped super villains from the <a href="/universe/Raft" title="Raft">Raft</a>, the explosive villain <a href="/universe/Nitro" title="Nitro" class="mw-redirect">Nitro</a> detonated himself killing the majority of the <a href="/universe/New_Warriors" title="New Warriors">New Warriors</a>, children at a nearby elementary school and other local residents. In the wake of the tragedy, the federal Superhuman Registration Act was passed, requiring all super-powered beings to register their identities and subject themselves to federally mandated standards. While Tony spearheaded the support for the Act, convincing <a href="/universe/Spider-Man" title="Spider-Man" class="mw-redirect">Spider-Man (Peter Parker)</a> to publicly unmask in support of the Act, Captain America led an underground resistance defending heroes’ rights of privacy. Stark was accepted the position of Director of S.H.I.E.L.D.
<p><br />
</p>
<a name="The_Hammer_Strikes_the_Shield" id="The_Hammer_Strikes_the_Shield"></a><h2> <span class="mw-headline"> The Hammer Strikes the Shield </span></h2>
When the alien Skrull’s Queen Veranke led an invasion of Earth, Earth’s defenses were disabled through a virus which ran through Tony’s Extremis-based powers, taking out all Stark-based technology. Although the heroes of Earth routed the Skrulls, it was “reformed” criminal Norman Osborn who slew Veranke and took the credit. Tony Stark was vilified for the failure of his technology to stop the Skrull invasion. S.H.I.E.L.D. was dismantled and Osborn put in charge of the replacement agency H.A.M.M.E.R. Osborn demanded Stark surrender the Superhuman Registration Database containing the secret identities of many heroes. Stark refused and loaded the database’s only copy into his brain. Evading capture by Osborn, Tony gradually wiped his mind. Tony was aided by <a href="/universe3zx/index.php?title=Maria_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maria Hill (page does not exist)">Maria Hill</a>, whom he sent to retrieve a hard drive containing a backup copy of his mind, and Pepper Hogan, whom he left in charge of Stark Industries and gifted with a suit of armor called Rescue, operated by an artificial intelligence named J.A.R.V.I.S. As Tony’s mind deteriorated he was finally assaulted in Dubai by the Iron Patriot-armored Osborn. By then Stark was virtually brain-dead and, as their battle was being televised, Osborn was forced to bring him in alive or risk being exposed for murdering a helpless man. Transferred to the custody of Dr. Donald Blake — actually Stark’s old friend Thor — Tony left directions which enabled his friends to restore his mind and awaken him from his coma. Iron Man returned to action in time to help in Osborn’s ultimate defeat.</div>
</div>
<p><br clear="all" />
</p>

<p><i><b>Iron Man</b></i> is a 2008 American <a href="/wiki/Superhero_film" title="Superhero film">superhero film</a> featuring the <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">Marvel Comics</a> character <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man" title="Iron Man">Iron Man</a>, produced by <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Studios" title="Marvel Studios">Marvel Studios</a> and distributed by <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount Pictures</a>.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_1"><a href="#endnote_1">1</a></sup> It is the first installment in the <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe" title="Marvel Cinematic Universe">Marvel Cinematic Universe</a>. The film was directed by <a href="/wiki/Jon_Favreau" title="Jon Favreau">Jon Favreau</a>, with a screenplay by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Fergus_and_Hawk_Ostby" title="Mark Fergus and Hawk Ostby">Mark Fergus and Hawk Ostby</a>, Art Marcum and Matt Holloway. It stars <a href="/wiki/Robert_Downey,_Jr." title="Robert Downey, Jr.">Robert Downey, Jr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terrence_Howard" title="Terrence Howard">Terrence Howard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bridges" title="Jeff Bridges">Jeff Bridges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Toub" title="Shaun Toub">Shaun Toub</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gwyneth_Paltrow" title="Gwyneth Paltrow">Gwyneth Paltrow</a>. In <i>Iron Man</i>, Tony Stark, an industrialist and master engineer, builds a <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man%27s_armor#Live-action_films" title="Iron Man's armor">powered exoskeleton</a> and becomes the technologically advanced <a href="/wiki/Superhero" title="Superhero">superhero</a> Iron Man.</p>
<p>The film had been in development since 1990 at <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" title="Universal Studios">Universal Pictures</a>, <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a>, or <a href="/wiki/New_Line_Cinema" title="New Line Cinema">New Line Cinema</a> at various times, before <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Studios" title="Marvel Studios">Marvel Studios</a> reacquired the rights in 2006. Marvel put the project in production as its first self-financed film, with Paramount Pictures as its distributor. Favreau signed on as director, aiming for a naturalistic feel, and he chose to shoot the film primarily in California, rejecting the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast</a> setting of the comics to differentiate the film from numerous superhero films set in New York City-esque environments. During filming, the actors were free to create their own dialogue because pre-production was focused on the story and action. Rubber and metal versions of the armors, created by <a href="/wiki/Stan_Winston" title="Stan Winston">Stan Winston</a>'s company, were mixed with <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated imagery</a> to create the title character.</p>
<p><i>Iron Man</i> premiered in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a> on April 14, 2008, and was released in theaters on May 2, 2008. The film was a critical and commercial success, grossing over $585.1 million, and garnering widespread critical acclaim, with Downey's performance as Tony Stark particularly praised. The <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute" title="American Film Institute">American Film Institute</a> selected the film as one of the ten best of the year. A sequel, <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_2" title="Iron Man 2">Iron Man 2</a></i>, was released on May 7, 2010, and another sequel, <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_3" title="Iron Man 3">Iron Man 3</a></i>, was released on May 3, 2013.</p>
<p></p>
