<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span></h2>
<p>Genius, billionaire, <a href="/wiki/Playboy_(lifestyle)" title="Playboy (lifestyle)">playboy</a>, and philanthropist, <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man" title="Iron Man">Tony Stark</a>, who has inherited the defense contractor <a href="/wiki/Stark_Industries" title="Stark Industries">Stark Industries</a> from his father, is in <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">war-torn Afghanistan</a> with his friend and <a href="/wiki/Civil-Military_Co-operation#Doctrine" title="Civil-Military Co-operation" class="mw-redirect">military liaison</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Colonel" title="Lieutenant Colonel" class="mw-redirect">Lieutenant Colonel</a> <a href="/wiki/War_Machine" title="War Machine">James Rhodes</a> to demonstrate the new "Jericho" <a href="/wiki/Cluster_bomb" title="Cluster bomb" class="mw-redirect">missile</a>. The convoy is ambushed and Stark is critically wounded by one of his own rocket propelled grenades. He is captured and imprisoned in a cave by the terrorist group the <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_(comics)#Films" title="Mandarin (comics)">Ten Rings</a>, and an <a href="/wiki/Electromagnet" title="Electromagnet">electromagnet</a> is grafted into his chest by fellow captive <a href="/wiki/Ho_Yinsen" title="Ho Yinsen">Yinsen</a> to keep the <a href="/wiki/Shrapnel_shell" title="Shrapnel shell">shrapnel</a> shell shards that wounded him from reaching his heart and killing him. Ten Rings leader Raza offers Stark freedom in exchange for building a Jericho missile for the group, but Tony and Yinsen agree Raza will not keep his word.</p>
<p>Stark and Yinsen secretly build a powerful electric generator called an <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man%27s_armor#Arc_reactor" title="Iron Man's armor">arc reactor</a> to power Stark's electromagnet, and then begin to secretly build a <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man%27s_armor#Live-action_films" title="Iron Man's armor">suit of armor</a> to be powered by the reactor, and to be used to escape. Although they keep the suit hidden almost to completion, the Ten Rings attack the workshop when they discover their intentions. Yinsen sacrifices himself to divert them while the suit powers up. The armored Stark battles his way out of the cave to find the dying Yinsen, then in anger burns the Ten Rings weapons and flies away, crashing in the desert and destroying the suit. After being rescued by Rhodes, Stark returns home and announces that his company will no longer manufacture weapons. <a href="/wiki/Iron_Monger" title="Iron Monger">Obadiah Stane</a>, his father's old partner and the company's manager, advises Stark that this may ruin Stark Industries and his father's legacy. In his home workshop, Stark builds an improved version of his suit, as well as a more powerful arc reactor for his chest. Personal assistant <a href="/wiki/Pepper_Potts" title="Pepper Potts">Pepper Potts</a> places the original reactor inside a small glass showcase. Though Stane requests details, Stark keeps his work to himself.</p>
<p>At a charity event held by Stark Industries, reporter <a href="/wiki/Christine_Everhart" title="Christine Everhart" class="mw-redirect">Christine Everhart</a> informs Stark that his company's weapons, including the Jericho, were recently delivered to the Ten Rings and are being used to attack Yinsen's home village, Gulmira. Stark also learns Stane is trying to replace him as head of the company. Enraged by these revelations, Stark dons his new armor and flies to Afghanistan, where he saves Yinsen's village. While flying home, Stark is shot at by two <a href="/wiki/F-22_Raptor" title="F-22 Raptor" class="mw-redirect">F-22 Raptor</a> fighter jets. He reveals his secret identity to Rhodes over the phone in an attempt to end the attack. Meanwhile, the Ten Rings gather the pieces of Stark's prototype suit and meet with Stane, who subdues Raza with a sonic device and has the rest of the group killed, before having a new suit <a href="/wiki/Reverse_engineering" title="Reverse engineering">reverse engineered</a> from the wreckage. Seeking to find any other weapons delivered to the Ten Rings, Stark sends Pepper to <a href="/wiki/Hacker_(computer_security)" title="Hacker (computer security)">hack</a> into the company computer system from Stane's office. She discovers Stane has been supplying the terrorists and hired the Ten Rings to kill Stark, but the group reneged. Potts meets with Agent <a href="/wiki/Phil_Coulson" title="Phil Coulson">Phil Coulson</a> of <a href="/wiki/S.H.I.E.L.D." title="S.H.I.E.L.D.">S.H.I.E.L.D.</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Counter-terrorism" title="Counter-terrorism">counter-terrorism</a> agency, to inform him of Stane's activities.</p>
<p>Stane's scientists cannot duplicate Stark's arc reactor so Stane ambushes Stark at home and takes his, though Stark manages to get to his original reactor to replace the taken one. Potts and several S.H.I.E.L.D. agents attempt to arrest Stane, but he dons his suit and attacks them. Stark fights Stane, but is outmatched without his new reactor to run his suit at full capacity. Stark lures Stane atop the Stark Industries building and instructs Potts to overload the large arc reactor there. This unleashes a massive electrical surge that causes Stane and his armor to fall into the exploding reactor, killing him. The next day, at a press conference, Stark admits to being the superhero the press has dubbed "Iron Man".</p>
<p>In a <a href="/wiki/Post-credits_scene" title="Post-credits scene">post-credits scene</a>, S.H.I.E.L.D. Director <a href="/wiki/Nick_Fury" title="Nick Fury">Nick Fury</a> visits Stark at home, telling him that Iron Man is not "the only superhero in the world", and explaining that he wants to discuss the "<a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">Avengers Initiative</a>".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Downey_Jr_at_Comic_Con_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Robert_Downey_Jr_at_Comic_Con_2007.jpg/170px-Robert_Downey_Jr_at_Comic_Con_2007.jpg" width="170" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Robert_Downey_Jr_at_Comic_Con_2007.jpg/255px-Robert_Downey_Jr_at_Comic_Con_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Robert_Downey_Jr_at_Comic_Con_2007.jpg/340px-Robert_Downey_Jr_at_Comic_Con_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="520" data-file-height="650" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Downey_Jr_at_Comic_Con_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Downey promoting the film at the 2007 <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con International</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Downey,_Jr." title="Robert Downey, Jr.">Robert Downey, Jr.</a> as <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man" title="Iron Man">Tony Stark / Iron Man</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>An <a href="/wiki/Industrialist" title="Industrialist" class="mw-redirect">industrialist</a>, genius inventor, and consummate playboy, he is CEO of <a href="/wiki/Stark_Industries" title="Stark Industries">Stark Industries</a> and a chief weapons manufacturer for the <a href="/wiki/U.S._military" title="U.S. military" class="mw-redirect">U.S. military</a>. Favreau had planned to cast a newcomer in the role,<sup id="cite_ref-DowneyUnknown_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DowneyUnknown-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> but ultimately chose Downey, a fan of the comic,<sup id="cite_ref-DowneyUSAToday_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DowneyUSAToday-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> because he felt the actor's past made him an appropriate choice for the part, explaing that "The best and worst moments of Robert's life have been in the public eye. He had to find an inner balance to overcome obstacles that went far beyond his career. That's Tony Stark. Robert brings a depth that goes beyond a comic book character who is having trouble in high school, or can't get the girl."<sup id="cite_ref-DowneyUSAToday_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DowneyUSAToday-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Favreau felt Downey could make Stark a "likable asshole," but also depict an authentic emotional journey once he won over the audience.<sup id="cite_ref-FavreauWonderCon2008_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FavreauWonderCon2008-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Downey had an office next to Favreau during pre-production, which allowed him greater involvement in the screenwriting process.<sup id="cite_ref-EmpireJuly2007_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EmpireJuly2007-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> He brought a deeper sense of humor to the film not present in previous drafts of the script.<sup id="cite_ref-EmpireApril2008_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EmpireApril2008-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Downey explained, "What I usually hate about these [superhero] movies [is] when suddenly the guy that you were digging turns into <a href="/wiki/Dudley_Do-Right" title="Dudley Do-Right">Dudley Do-Right</a>, and then you're supposed to buy into all his 'Let's go do some good!' That <a href="/wiki/Eliot_Ness" title="Eliot Ness">Eliot Ness</a>-in-a-cape-type thing. What was really important to me was to not have him change so much that he's unrecognizable. When someone used to be a schmuck and they're not anymore, hopefully they still have a sense of humor."<sup id="cite_ref-FavreauStarkQuote_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FavreauStarkQuote-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> To prepare, Downey spent five days a week <a href="/wiki/Weight_training" title="Weight training">weight training</a> and practiced martial arts to get into shape,<sup id="cite_ref-DowneyUSAToday_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DowneyUSAToday-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> which he said benefited him because "it's hard not to have a personality meltdown [...] after about several hours in that suit. I'm calling up every therapeutic moment I can think of to just get through the day."<sup id="cite_ref-pump_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pump-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Terrence_Howard,_USAF.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Terrence_Howard%2C_USAF.jpg/170px-Terrence_Howard%2C_USAF.jpg" width="170" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Terrence_Howard%2C_USAF.jpg/255px-Terrence_Howard%2C_USAF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Terrence_Howard%2C_USAF.jpg/340px-Terrence_Howard%2C_USAF.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1068" data-file-height="1449" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Terrence_Howard,_USAF.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Howard preparing for the role by riding an <a href="/wiki/F-16_Fighting_Falcon" title="F-16 Fighting Falcon" class="mw-redirect">F-16</a> flight simulator.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Terrence_Howard" title="Terrence Howard">Terrence Howard</a> as <a href="/wiki/War_Machine" title="War Machine">Lt. Colonel James "Rhodey" Rhodes</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>A friend of Stark's, and the liaison between Stark Industries and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a> in the department of acquisitions, specifically weapons development. Favreau cast Howard because he felt he could play <a href="/wiki/War_Machine" title="War Machine">War Machine</a> in a sequel.<sup id="cite_ref-trilogy_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trilogy-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Howard prepared for the role by visiting <a href="/wiki/Nellis_Air_Force_Base" title="Nellis Air Force Base">Nellis Air Force Base</a> on March 16, 2007, where he ate with the pilots and observed <a href="/wiki/HH-60_Pave_Hawk" title="HH-60 Pave Hawk" class="mw-redirect">HH-60 Pave Hawk</a> rescue helicopters and <a href="/wiki/F-22_Raptor" title="F-22 Raptor" class="mw-redirect">F-22 Raptors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HowardNellis_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HowardNellis-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> While Rhodes is roguish in the comics after he met Stark, his earlier disciplinarian character forms <a href="/wiki/Double_act" title="Double act">a dynamic</a> with Stark, and he is unsure whether or not Stark's actions are acceptable. "Rhodey is completely disgusted with the way Tony has lived his life, but at a certain point he realizes that perhaps there is a different way," Howard said. "Whose life is the right way; is it the strict military life, or the life of an independent?"<sup id="cite_ref-pump_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pump-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Howard and his father are Iron Man fans, partly because Rhodes was one of the few black superheroes when he was a child.<sup id="cite_ref-RhodesFirst_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RhodesFirst-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> He was a Downey fan since he saw him in <i><a href="/wiki/Weird_Science_(film)" title="Weird Science (film)">Weird Science</a></i>, and the two competed physically on set.<sup id="cite_ref-HowardCompete_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HowardCompete-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bridges" title="Jeff Bridges">Jeff Bridges</a> as <a href="/wiki/Iron_Monger" title="Iron Monger">Obadiah Stane</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>Stark's business second-in-command. Bridges read the comics as a boy and liked Favreau's modern, realistic approach. He shaved his head, something he had wanted to do for some time, and grew a beard for the role. Bridges <a href="/wiki/Google_(verb)" title="Google (verb)">googled</a> the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Obadiah" title="Book of Obadiah">Book of Obadiah</a>, and was surprised to learn retribution is a major theme in that particular book of the Bible, something which Stane represents.<sup id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Many of Stane's scenes were cut out to focus more on Stark, but the writers felt Bridges's performance allowed the application of "less is more".<sup id="cite_ref-BridgesCut_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BridgesCut-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shaun_Toub" title="Shaun Toub">Shaun Toub</a> as <a href="/wiki/Ho_Yinsen" title="Ho Yinsen">Yinsen</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>Stark's fellow captive. In the comics, Yinsen is a Chinese physicist, but in the film, he comes from an Afghan village called Gulmira, which is one of the aspects of the modernization of the Iron Man mythos for the film.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gwyneth_Paltrow" title="Gwyneth Paltrow">Gwyneth Paltrow</a> as <a href="/wiki/Pepper_Potts" title="Pepper Potts">Pepper Potts</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>Stark's personal assistant and budding love interest. Paltrow asked Marvel to send her any comics that they would consider relevant to her understanding of the character, who she considered to be very smart, levelheaded, and grounded. She said she liked "the fact that there's a sexuality that's not blatant." Favreau wanted Potts' and Stark's relationship to be reminiscent of a 1940s comedy, something which Paltrow considered to be fun in a sexy, yet innocent way.<sup id="cite_ref-Paltrow_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paltrow-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<p>Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Faran_Tahir" title="Faran Tahir">Faran Tahir</a> appears as Raza, the leader of the Ten Rings; <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bettany" title="Paul Bettany">Paul Bettany</a> voices <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Jarvis#J.A.R.V.I.S." title="Edwin Jarvis">J.A.R.V.I.S.</a>, Stark's personal <a href="/wiki/Artificial_Intelligence" title="Artificial Intelligence" class="mw-redirect">AI</a> system; <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Bibb" title="Leslie Bibb">Leslie Bibb</a> portrays <a href="/wiki/Christine_Everhart" title="Christine Everhart" class="mw-redirect">Christine Everhart</a>, a reporter for <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i>; and <a href="/wiki/Clark_Gregg" title="Clark Gregg">Clark Gregg</a> appears as <a href="/wiki/Phil_Coulson" title="Phil Coulson">Phil Coulson</a>, an agent of <a href="/wiki/S.H.I.E.L.D." title="S.H.I.E.L.D.">S.H.I.E.L.D.</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IMEbertReview_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMEbertReview-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Will_Lyman" title="Will Lyman">Will Lyman</a> provides the voiceover during the opening award ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyman_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyman-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Samuel_L._Jackson" title="Samuel L. Jackson">Samuel L. Jackson</a> <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">cameos</a> as <a href="/wiki/Nick_Fury" title="Nick Fury">Nick Fury</a>, director of S.H.I.E.L.D., in a <a href="/wiki/Post-credits_scene" title="Post-credits scene">post-credits scene</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-samueljacksoncameo_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-samueljacksoncameo-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Jackson's face was previously used as the model for that of the <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Marvel" title="Ultimate Marvel">Ultimate Marvel</a> imprint <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Nick_Fury" title="Ultimate Nick Fury">version of Nick Fury</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JacksonUltimate_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JacksonUltimate-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Other cameos in the film include: <a href="/wiki/Stan_Lee" title="Stan Lee">Stan Lee</a> as himself, being mistaken for <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Hefner" title="Hugh Hefner">Hugh Hefner</a> by Stark at a party;<sup id="cite_ref-StanLee_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanLee-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> director <a href="/wiki/Jon_Favreau" title="Jon Favreau">Jon Favreau</a> as <a href="/wiki/Happy_Hogan" title="Happy Hogan">Happy Hogan</a>, Stark's <a href="/wiki/Bodyguard" title="Bodyguard">bodyguard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chauffeur" title="Chauffeur">chauffeur</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-EmpireApril2008_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EmpireApril2008-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> [Tom Morello]], who also provides additional guitar music for the film, as a terrorist guard;<sup id="cite_ref-Morello_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morello-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jim_Cramer" title="Jim Cramer">Jim Cramer</a> as himself.<sup id="cite_ref-Cramer_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cramer-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ghostface_Killah" title="Ghostface Killah">Ghostface Killah</a> had a cameo in a scene where Stark briefly stays in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>, but the scene was cut from the theatrical release for pacing reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-depth_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-depth-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width: 33%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"We worked with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Crichton" title="Michael Crichton">Michael Crichton</a>'s researchers to find a grounded realistic way to deal with the suit. The idea was he needed the suit to stay alive. He's the same guy we used with <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2" title="Spider-Man 2">Spider-Man 2</a></i> to come up with <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Octopus" title="Doctor Octopus">Doc Ock</a>'s inhibitor chips and what the arms are made of and how they work. [...] <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_(comics)" title="Mandarin (comics)">Mandarin</a> was an Indonesian terrorist who masqueraded as a rich playboy who Tony knew."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—Alfred Gough on his draft for Nick Cassavetes' and New Line's aborted version<sup id="cite_ref-GoughQuote_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoughQuote-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>In April 1990, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" title="Universal Studios">Universal Studios</a> bought the rights to develop <i>Iron Man</i> for the big screen.<sup id="cite_ref-Universal_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Universal-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Gordon" title="Stuart Gordon">Stuart Gordon</a> was to direct a low-budget film based on the property,<sup id="cite_ref-pump_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pump-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> but by February 1996, <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a> had acquired the rights from Universal.<sup id="cite_ref-Fox_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> In January 1997, <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Cage" title="Nicolas Cage">Nicolas Cage</a> expressed interest in portraying the lead role in a potential film,<sup id="cite_ref-Cage_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cage-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> while in September 1998, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Cruise" title="Tom Cruise">Tom Cruise</a> had expressed interest in producing as well as starring in the film debut of Iron Man.<sup id="cite_ref-Cruise_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cruise-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Vintar" title="Jeff Vintar">Jeff Vintar</a> and Iron Man co-creator <a href="/wiki/Stan_Lee" title="Stan Lee">Stan Lee</a> co-wrote a story for Fox, which Vintar adapted into a screenplay, and included a new science-fiction origin for the character, and featured <a href="/wiki/MODOK" title="MODOK">MODOK</a> as the villain. <a href="/wiki/Tom_Rothman" title="Tom Rothman" class="mw-redirect">Tom Rothman</a>, President of Production at Fox, credited the screenplay with finally making him understand the character. In May 1999, Jeffrey Caine was hired to rewrite Vintar and Lee's script,<sup id="cite_ref-archive_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> while in October 1999, <a href="/wiki/Quentin_Tarantino" title="Quentin Tarantino">Quentin Tarantino</a> was approached to write and direct the film.<sup id="cite_ref-Tarantino_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tarantino-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Fox eventually sold the rights to <a href="/wiki/New_Line_Cinema" title="New Line Cinema">New Line Cinema</a> the following December, reasoning that although the Vintar/Lee script was strong, the studio had too many Marvel superheroes in development, and "we can't make them all."<sup id="cite_ref-NewLine_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewLine-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> By July 2000, the film was being written for New Line<sup id="cite_ref-NewLine2_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewLine2-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/Ted_Elliott_(screenwriter)" title="Ted Elliott (screenwriter)">Ted Elliott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terry_Rossio" title="Terry Rossio">Terry Rossio</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-archive_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_McCanlies" title="Tim McCanlies">Tim McCanlies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-McCanliesWriting_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCanliesWriting-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> McCanlies's script used the idea of a <a href="/wiki/Nick_Fury" title="Nick Fury">Nick Fury</a> cameo to set up his own film.<sup id="cite_ref-archive_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2001, New Line entered talks with <a href="/wiki/Joss_Whedon" title="Joss Whedon">Joss Whedon</a>, a fan of the character, to direct,<sup id="cite_ref-WhedonDirecting_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhedonDirecting-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> and in December 2002, McCanlies had turned in a completed script.<sup id="cite_ref-McCanliesCompleted_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCanliesCompleted-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 2004, the studio attached director <a href="/wiki/Nick_Cassavetes" title="Nick Cassavetes">Nick Cassavetes</a> to the project for a target 2006 release.<sup id="cite_ref-Cassavetes_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cassavetes-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Screenplay drafts were written by <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Gough" title="Alfred Gough">Alfred Gough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miles_Millar" title="Miles Millar">Miles Millar</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Hayter" title="David Hayter">David Hayter</a>, and pitted Iron Man against his father <a href="/wiki/Howard_Stark" title="Howard Stark">Howard Stark</a>, who becomes <a href="/wiki/War_Machine" title="War Machine">War Machine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NewLineScreenplays_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewLineScreenplays-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After two years of unsuccessful development, and the deal with Cassavetes falling through, <a href="/wiki/New_Line_Cinema" title="New Line Cinema">New Line Cinema</a> returned the film rights to Marvel.<sup id="cite_ref-NewLineScreenplays_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewLineScreenplays-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2005, <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Studios" title="Marvel Studios">Marvel Studios</a> worked to start development from scratch,<sup id="cite_ref-MarvelDevelopment_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarvelDevelopment-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> and announced <i>Iron Man</i> as their first independent feature, as the character was their only major one not already depicted in live action.<sup id="cite_ref-EmpireJuly2007_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EmpireJuly2007-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> According to associate producer Jeremy Latcham, "we went after about 30 writers and they all passed", saying they were uninterested in the project due to both the relative obscurity of the character and it being a solely Marvel production. Even the rewrites when the film had a script lead to many refusals.<sup id="cite_ref-MCUDocumentary_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCUDocumentary-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-production">Pre-production</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Len_Wiseman" title="Len Wiseman">Len Wiseman</a> had been in negotiations to direct,<sup id="cite_ref-Wiseman_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wiseman-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> before <a href="/wiki/Jon_Favreau" title="Jon Favreau">Jon Favreau</a> was hired in April 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-FavreauMarcumHolloway_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FavreauMarcumHolloway-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Favreau had wanted to work with Marvel producer <a href="/wiki/Avi_Arad" title="Avi Arad">Avi Arad</a> on another film after they both worked on <i><a href="/wiki/Daredevil_(film)" title="Daredevil (film)">Daredevil</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-EmpireJuly2007_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EmpireJuly2007-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Favreau celebrated getting the job by going on a diet, and lost seventy pounds.<sup id="cite_ref-pump_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pump-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The director found the opportunity to create a politically ambitious "ultimate spy movie" in <i>Iron Man</i>, citing inspiration from <a href="/wiki/Tom_Clancy" title="Tom Clancy">Tom Clancy</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a>, and <a href="/wiki/RoboCop" title="RoboCop">RoboCop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Inspiration_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inspiration-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Favreau described his approach as similar to an <a href="/wiki/Independent_film" title="Independent film">independent film</a> — "[i]f <a href="/wiki/Robert_Altman" title="Robert Altman">Robert Altman</a> had directed <i><a href="/wiki/Superman_(1978_film)" title="Superman (1978 film)">Superman</a></i>"<sup id="cite_ref-EmpireJuly2007_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EmpireJuly2007-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> — and also cited <i><a href="/wiki/Batman_Begins" title="Batman Begins">Batman Begins</a></i> as an inspiration.<sup id="cite_ref-sauron_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sauron-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> He wanted to make <i>Iron Man</i> a story of an adult man literally reinventing himself after discovering the world is far more complex than he originally believed.<sup id="cite_ref-FavreauWants_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FavreauWants-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Favreau changed the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> origin of the character to Afghanistan, as he did not want to do a <a href="/wiki/Period_piece" title="Period piece">period piece</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-trilogy_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trilogy-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Arthur Marcum and Matt Holloway where hired to write the script,<sup id="cite_ref-FavreauMarcumHolloway_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FavreauMarcumHolloway-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> while Mark Fergus and Hawk Ostby wrote another version, with Favreau compiling both team's scripts,<sup id="cite_ref-FergusOstby_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FergusOstby-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/John_August" title="John August">John August</a> then 'polishing' the combined version.<sup id="cite_ref-August_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-August-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Comic book staff <a href="/wiki/Mark_Millar" title="Mark Millar">Mark Millar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Michael_Bendis" title="Brian Michael Bendis">Brian Michael Bendis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Quesada" title="Joe Quesada">Joe Quesada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Brevoort" title="Tom Brevoort">Tom Brevoort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Axel_Alonso" title="Axel Alonso">Axel Alonso</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Macchio_(comics)" title="Ralph Macchio (comics)">Ralph Macchio</a> were also called upon by Favreau to give advice on the script.<sup id="cite_ref-thinktank_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thinktank-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Favreau, while "trying to [make] the character of genius billionaire Tony Stark... seem real," took Robert Downey Jr.'s suggestion for a meeting with <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">Elon Musk</a>, the founder of <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">SpaceX</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla</a>. Favreau felt "Downey was right", calling Musk "a paragon of enthusiasm, good humor and curiosity — a Renaissance man in an era that needs them."<sup id="cite_ref-Musk_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Musk-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Choosing a villain was difficult, because Favreau felt Iron Man's archnemesis, the <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_(comics)" title="Mandarin (comics)">Mandarin</a>, would not feel realistic, especially after Mark Millar gave his opinion on the script.<sup id="cite_ref-thinktank_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thinktank-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> He felt only in a sequel, with an altered tone, would the fantasy of the Mandarin's rings be appropriate.<sup id="cite_ref-mandarin_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mandarin-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> The decision to push him into the background is comparable to <a href="/wiki/Sauron" title="Sauron">Sauron</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-sauron_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sauron-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Palpatine" title="Palpatine">Palpatine</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-mandarin_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mandarin-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Favreau also wanted Iron Man to face a giant enemy. The switch from Mandarin to Obadiah Stane was done after Bridges was cast,<sup id="cite_ref-depth_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-depth-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> with Stane originally intended to become a villain in the sequel.<sup id="cite_ref-thinktank_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thinktank-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Crimson_Dynamo" title="Crimson Dynamo">Crimson Dynamo</a> was also a villain in early drafts of the script.<sup id="cite_ref-EmpireApril2008_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EmpireApril2008-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Favreau felt it was important to include intentional <a href="/wiki/In-joke" title="In-joke">inside references</a> for fans of the comics, such as giving the two fighter jets that attack Iron Man the <a href="/wiki/Call_sign" title="Call sign">call signs</a> of "Whiplash 1" and "Whiplash 2," a reference to the comic book villain <a href="/wiki/Blacklash" title="Blacklash" class="mw-redirect">Whiplash</a>, and including <a href="/wiki/Captain_America" title="Captain America">Captain America</a>'s shield in Stark's workshop.<sup id="cite_ref-EasterEggs_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EasterEggs-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The post-credits sequence that introduces <a href="/wiki/Samuel_L._Jackson" title="Samuel L. Jackson">Samuel L. Jackson</a> as <a href="/wiki/Nick_Fury" title="Nick Fury">Nick Fury</a> was written by comics writer <a href="/wiki/Brian_Michael_Bendis" title="Brian Michael Bendis">Brian Michael Bendis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-samueljacksoncameo_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-samueljacksoncameo-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span></h3>
<p>Production was based in the former <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hughes" title="Howard Hughes">Hughes Company</a> soundstages in <a href="/wiki/Playa_Vista,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Playa Vista, Los Angeles, California" class="mw-redirect">Playa Vista, Los Angeles, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PlayaVista_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PlayaVista-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hughes" title="Howard Hughes">Howard Hughes</a> was one of the inspirations for the comic book, and the filmmakers acknowledged the coincidence that they would film Iron Man creating the flying Mark III where the <a href="/wiki/Hughes_H-4_Hercules" title="Hughes H-4 Hercules">Hughes H-4 Hercules</a> was built.<sup id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Favreau rejected the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast</a> setting of the comic books because many superhero films had already been set there.<sup id="cite_ref-trilogy_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trilogy-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Filming began on March 12, 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-FilmingBegins_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FilmingBegins-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> with the first few weeks spent on Stark's captivity in Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-FirstWeeks_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FirstWeeks-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> The cave where Stark is imprisoned was a 150- to 200-yard (150–200 m) long set, which had movable forks in the caverns to allow greater freedom for the film's crew.<sup id="cite_ref-trilogy_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trilogy-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Production_designer" title="Production designer">Production designer</a> <a href="/wiki/J._Michael_Riva" title="J. Michael Riva">J. Michael Riva</a> saw footage of a <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> fighter in Afghanistan, and saw the cold breath as he spoke: realizing remote caves are actually very cold, Riva placed an air conditioning system in the set. He also sought Downey's advice about makeshift objects in prison, such as a sock being used to make tea.<sup id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Afterwards, Stark's capture was filmed at <a href="/wiki/Lone_Pine,_California" title="Lone Pine, California">Lone Pine</a>, and other exterior scenes in Afghanistan were filmed at <a href="/wiki/Olancha" title="Olancha" class="mw-redirect">Olancha</a> Sand Dunes, where the crew endured two days of 40 to 60-mile per hour (60 to 100 km/h) winds.<sup id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Filming at <a href="/wiki/Edwards_Air_Force_Base" title="Edwards Air Force Base">Edwards Air Force Base</a> began in mid-April,<sup id="cite_ref-EdwardsBegins_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EdwardsBegins-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> and ended on May 2.<sup id="cite_ref-EdwardsEnds_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EdwardsEnds-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> Exterior shots of Stark's home were digitally added to footage of <a href="/wiki/Point_Dume" title="Point Dume">Point Dume</a> in <a href="/wiki/Malibu,_California" title="Malibu, California">Malibu</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-depth_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-depth-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> while the interior was built at Playa Vista, where Favreau and Riva aimed to make Stark's home look less futuristic and more "<a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/grease_monkey" class="extiw" title="wikt:grease monkey">grease monkey</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Filming concluded on June 25, 2007, at <a href="/wiki/Caesars_Palace" title="Caesars Palace">Caesars Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada" class="mw-redirect">Las Vegas, Nevada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FilmingEnds_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FilmingEnds-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Favreau, a newcomer to action films, remarked, "I'm shocked that I [was] on schedule. I thought that there were going to be many curveballs". He hired "people who are good at creating action", so "the human story [felt] like it belongs to the comic book genre".<sup id="cite_ref-pump_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pump-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>There was much <a href="/wiki/Improvisation" title="Improvisation">improvisation</a> in dialogue scenes, because the script was not completed when filming began (the filmmakers had focused on the story making sense and planning the action). Favreau acknowledged that improvisation would make the film feel more natural. Some scenes were shot with two cameras to capture lines said on the spot. Multiple takes were done, as Downey wanted to try something new each time.<sup id="cite_ref-depth_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-depth-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> It was Downey's idea to have Stark hold a <a href="/wiki/News_conference" title="News conference">news conference</a> on the floor,<sup id="cite_ref-pump_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pump-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> and he created the speech Stark makes when demonstrating the Jericho weapon.<sup id="cite_ref-FavreauWonderCon2008_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FavreauWonderCon2008-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brian_Michael_Bendis" title="Brian Michael Bendis">Brian Michael Bendis</a> wrote three pages of dialogue for the Nick Fury cameo scene, with the filmmakers choosing the best lines for filming.<sup id="cite_ref-thinktank_47-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thinktank-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> The cameo was filmed with a skeleton crew in order to keep it a secret, but rumors appeared on the Internet only days later. Marvel Studios's Kevin Feige subsequently had the scene removed from all preview prints in order to maintain the surprise and keep fans guessing.<sup id="cite_ref-CameoRemoved_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CameoRemoved-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-production">Post-production</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ironmonger_2008film.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c7/Ironmonger_2008film.jpg/220px-Ironmonger_2008film.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c7/Ironmonger_2008film.jpg/330px-Ironmonger_2008film.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c7/Ironmonger_2008film.jpg/440px-Ironmonger_2008film.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="300" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ironmonger_2008film.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A scale model of the "Iron Monger" suit.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Favreau wanted the film to be believable by showing the construction of the suit in its three stages.<sup id="cite_ref-trilogy_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trilogy-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stan_Winston" title="Stan Winston">Stan Winston</a>, a fan of the comic book, and his company built metal and rubber versions of the armors. They had previously worked on Favreau's <i><a href="/wiki/Zathura_(film)" title="Zathura (film)">Zathura</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Favreau's main concern with the effects was whether the transition between the computer-generated and practical costumes would be too obvious.<sup id="cite_ref-FavreauEffectsConcerns_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FavreauEffectsConcerns-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic" title="Industrial Light &amp; Magic">Industrial Light &amp; Magic</a> (ILM) was hired to create the bulk of the visual effects, with additional work being completed by <a href="/wiki/The_Orphanage_(company)" title="The Orphanage (company)">The Orphanage</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Embassy_Visual_Effects" title="The Embassy Visual Effects">The Embassy</a>; Favreau trusted ILM after seeing <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: At World's End">Pirates of the Caribbean: At World's End</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Transformers_(film)" title="Transformers (film)">Transformers</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> The Mark I design was intended to look like it was built from spare parts. The back is less armored than the front, because Stark would use his resources for a forward attack. It also foreshadows the design of Stane's armor. A single 90-pound (41&#160;kg) version was built, causing concern when a stuntman fell over inside it, though both the stuntman and the suit were unscathed. The armor was also designed to only have its top half worn at times.<sup id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> The Embassy created a digital version of the Mark I.<sup id="cite_ref-Embassy_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Embassy-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Stan Winston Studios built a 10-foot (3.0&#160;m), 800-pound (360&#160;kg) animatronic version of "<a href="/wiki/Iron_Monger" title="Iron Monger">Iron Monger</a>" (Obadiah Stane),<sup id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_13-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> a name which Obadiah Stane calls Tony Stark and himself earlier in the film as a reference, but is never actually used for the suit itself in the film. The animatronic required five operators for the arm, and was built on a <a href="/wiki/Gimbal" title="Gimbal">gimbal</a> to simulate walking.<sup id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_13-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Scale_model" title="Scale model">scale model</a> was used for the shots of it being built.<sup id="cite_ref-depth_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-depth-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Mark II resembles an airplane prototype, with visible flaps.<sup id="cite_ref-depth_23-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-depth-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Iron Man comic book artist <a href="/wiki/Adi_Granov" title="Adi Granov">Adi Granov</a> designed the Mark III with illustrator Phil Saunders.<sup id="cite_ref-GranovSaunders_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GranovSaunders-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Granov's designs were the primary inspiration for the film's, and he came on board the film after he recognized his work on Jon Favreau's MySpace page.<sup id="cite_ref-sauron_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sauron-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Saunders streamlined Granov's concept art, making it stealthier and less cartoonish in its proportions.<sup id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_13-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Sometimes, Downey would only wear the helmet, sleeves and chest of the costume over a <a href="/wiki/Motion_capture" title="Motion capture">motion capture</a> suit.<sup id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_13-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> For shots of the Mark III flying, it was animated to look realistic by taking off slowly, and landing quickly. To generate shots of Iron Man and the <a href="/wiki/F-22_Raptor" title="F-22 Raptor" class="mw-redirect">F-22 Raptors</a> battling, cameras were flown in the air to provide reference for physics, wind and frost on the lenses.<sup id="cite_ref-MarkIIIFlying_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarkIIIFlying-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> For further study of the physics of flying, skydivers were filmed in a vertical <a href="/wiki/Wind_tunnel" title="Wind tunnel">wind tunnel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WindTunnel_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WindTunnel-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Phil Saunders created <a href="/wiki/Concept_art" title="Concept art">concept art</a> for the <a href="/wiki/War_Machine" title="War Machine">War Machine</a> armor and said that it was originally intended to be used in the film but was "cut from the script about halfway through pre-production." Saunders said that the War Machine armor "was going to be called the Mark IV armor and would have had weaponized swap-out parts that would be worn over the original Mark III armor," and that it "would have been worn by Tony Stark in the final battle sequence."<sup id="cite_ref-WarMachine_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WarMachine-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_(soundtrack)" title="Iron Man (soundtrack)">Iron Man (soundtrack)</a></div>
<p>Composer <a href="/wiki/Ramin_Djawadi" title="Ramin Djawadi">Ramin Djawadi</a>, an Iron Man fan who still has issues of the comic from the late 1970s, has also been into heavy metal music since the early 1990s. While he normally composes after watching an <a href="/wiki/Assembly_cut" title="Assembly cut" class="mw-redirect">assembly cut</a>, Djawadi began work after seeing the <a href="/wiki/Teaser_trailer" title="Teaser trailer" class="mw-redirect">teaser trailer</a>. Favreau clearly envisioned a focus on "heavy" guitar in the score, and Djawadi composed the music on that instrument before arranging it for orchestra. The composer said Downey's performance inspired the several Iron Man themes (for his different moods), as well as Stark's playboy <a href="/wiki/Leitmotif" title="Leitmotif">leitmotif</a>. Djawadi's favorite of the Iron Man themes is the "kickass" because of its "rhythmic pattern that is a hook on its own. Very much like a machine." The other themes are "not so much character based, but rather plot based that carry you through the movie".<sup id="cite_ref-Music_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Music-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tom_Morello" title="Tom Morello">Tom Morello</a> of <a href="/wiki/Rage_Against_the_Machine" title="Rage Against the Machine">Rage Against the Machine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audioslave" title="Audioslave">Audioslave</a>, contributed additional guitar work to the film's soundtrack.<sup id="cite_ref-Morello_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morello-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span></h2>
<p>The premiere was held at the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Union" title="Greater Union" class="mw-redirect">Greater Union</a> theater at <a href="/wiki/George_Street,_Sydney" title="George Street, Sydney">George Street, Sydney</a>, on April 14, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Premiere_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Premiere-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> The film was released in the United State on May 2, 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-USRelease_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USRelease-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> while the international release was pushed up to April 30, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-InternationalRelease_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InternationalRelease-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Downey_Jr-2008.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Robert_Downey_Jr-2008.JPG/170px-Robert_Downey_Jr-2008.JPG" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Robert_Downey_Jr-2008.JPG/255px-Robert_Downey_Jr-2008.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Robert_Downey_Jr-2008.JPG/340px-Robert_Downey_Jr-2008.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3872" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Downey_Jr-2008.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Downey promoting the film in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Marvel and Paramount modeled their marketing campaign for <i>Iron Man</i> on that of <i><a href="/wiki/Transformers_(film)" title="Transformers (film)">Transformers</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-transformers_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transformers-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sega" title="Sega">Sega</a> released an <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_(video_game)" title="Iron Man (video game)">video game</a> based on the film, which included other iterations of the character.<sup id="cite_ref-VideoGame_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VideoGame-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> A 30-second spot for the film aired during a <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLII" title="Super Bowl XLII">Super Bowl XLII</a> break.<sup id="cite_ref-SuperBowl_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SuperBowl-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> 6,400 <a href="/wiki/7-Eleven" title="7-Eleven">7-Eleven</a> stores in the United States helped promote the film, and <a href="/wiki/LG_Group" title="LG Group" class="mw-redirect">LG Group</a> also made a deal with Paramount.<sup id="cite_ref-transformers_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transformers-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hasbro" title="Hasbro">Hasbro</a> created figures of armors from the film, as well as <a href="/wiki/Titanium_Man" title="Titanium Man">Titanium Man</a> (who appears in the video game) and the <a href="/wiki/Hulkbuster_Armor_MK_II" title="Hulkbuster Armor MK II" class="mw-redirect">armor from the <i>World War Hulk</i> comics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hasbro_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hasbro-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Worldwide, <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">Audi</a> promoted the film. Jon Favreau was set to direct a commercial for the fast-food chain, as <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bay" title="Michael Bay">Michael Bay</a> did for <i>Transformers</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-transformers_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transformers-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> In the film, Tony Stark drives an <a href="/wiki/Audi_R8_(road_car)" title="Audi R8 (road car)" class="mw-redirect">Audi R8</a>, and also has an "American cheeseburger" from Burger King after his rescue from Afghanistan, as part of the studio's <a href="/wiki/Product_placement" title="Product placement">product placement</a> deal with the respective companies. Three other vehicles, the <a href="/wiki/Audi_S6" title="Audi S6">Audi S6</a> sedan, <a href="/wiki/Audi_A5" title="Audi A5">Audi S5</a> sports coupe and the <a href="/wiki/Audi_Q7" title="Audi Q7">Audi Q7</a> SUV, also appear in the film.<sup id="cite_ref-Audi_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Audi-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Audi created a tie-in website, as <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> did for <i>Transformers</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-transformers_68-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transformers-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle Corporation</a> also promoted the film on its site.<sup id="cite_ref-Oracle_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oracle-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Several <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_tie-in_comics" title="Marvel Cinematic Universe tie-in comics">tie-in comics</a> were released for the film.<sup id="cite_ref-Comics_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comics-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span></h3>
<p><span id="DVD"></span><span id="Video"></span> The film was released on DVD and <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a> on September 30, 2008, in North America, and October 27, 2008 in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-HomeMediaRelease_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HomeMediaRelease-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> DVD sales were very successful, selling over 4 million copies the first week and generating a gross of over US$93 million.<sup id="cite_ref-TheNumbers_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheNumbers-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rediff_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rediff-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> There were a total of 9 million copies sold and an accumulated total sales of over $160 million (not including Blu-ray).<sup id="cite_ref-TheNumbers_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheNumbers-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> For the home releases of the film, the image on the newspaper Stark reads before he announces he is Iron Man had to be altered because of amateur photographer Ronnie Adams filing a lawsuit against Paramount and Marvel for using his on-location spy photo in the scene.<sup id="cite_ref-AdamsPhoto_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AdamsPhoto-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Wal-Mart</a>-exclusive release included a preview of <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man:_Armored_Adventures" title="Iron Man: Armored Adventures">Iron Man: Armored Adventures</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-WalMart_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WalMart-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The film was also collected in a 10-disc <a href="/wiki/Box_set" title="Box set">box set</a> titled <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_films#Home_Media" title="List of Marvel Cinematic Universe films">Marvel Cinematic Universe: Phase One – Avengers Assembled</a></i> which includes all of the "<a href="/wiki/List_of_Marvel_Cinematic_Universe_films#Phase_One" title="List of Marvel Cinematic Universe films">Phase One</a>" films in the Marvel Cinematic Universe.<sup id="cite_ref-PhaseOneSetAnnounced_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PhaseOneSetAnnounced-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> It was released on April 2, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-PhaseOneSetDelayed_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PhaseOneSetDelayed-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span></h3>
<p><i>Iron Man</i> earned $318.4 million in North America and $266.8 million in other territories, for a worldwide gross of $585.1 million.<sup id="cite_ref-boxmojo_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boxmojo-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>North America</dt>
</dl>
<p>In its opening weekend, <i>Iron Man</i> grossed $98,618,668 in 4,105 theaters in the United States and Canada, ranking No. 1 at the box office,<sup id="cite_ref-mojoweek_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mojoweek-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> giving it the eleventh biggest-opening weekend at the time,<sup id="cite_ref-mojoweekend_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mojoweekend-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> ninth-widest release in terms of theaters,<sup id="cite_ref-mojotheaters_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mojotheaters-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> and the third highest-grossing opening weekend of 2008 behind <i><a href="/wiki/Indiana_Jones_and_the_Kingdom_of_the_Crystal_Skull" title="Indiana Jones and the Kingdom of the Crystal Skull">Indiana Jones and the Kingdom of the Crystal Skull</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i>. It grossed $35.2 million on its first day, giving it the thirteenth biggest-opening day at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-mojoday_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mojoday-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Iron Man</i> had the second-best premiere for a non-sequel, behind <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_(2002_film)" title="Spider-Man (2002 film)">Spider-Man</a></i>, and the fourth biggest-opening for a superhero film.<sup id="cite_ref-forbessuperhero_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbessuperhero-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Iron Man</i> was also the No. 1 film in the U.S. and Canada in its second weekend, grossing $51.1 million,<sup id="cite_ref-mojoweek_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mojoweek-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> giving it the twelfth-best second weekend and the fifth-best for a non-sequel.<sup id="cite_ref-mojosecond_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mojosecond-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> On June 18, 2008, <i>Iron Man</i> became that year's first film to pass the $300 million mark for the domestic box office.<sup id="cite_ref-mojo300_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mojo300-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-news300_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news300-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response"><span id="Critics"></span><span id="Critical_reception"></span>Critical response</span></h3>
<p>In May 2008, <i>Iron Man</i> was identified as the "best-reviewed film of the year so far" by Jen Yamato of review aggregator <i><a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a></i>, with the site reporting that at that time the film had received a rating of 95% based on 107 reviews, a rating that held its place to January 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Best_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Best-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">review aggregator</a> website <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> reported a 93% approval rating with an average rating of 7.6/10 based on 242 reviews. The website's consensus reads, "Director Jon Favreau and star Robert Downey make this smart, high impact superhero movie one that even non-comics fans can enjoy."<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a> gave the film a <a href="/wiki/Standard_score" title="Standard score">normalized</a> <a href="/wiki/Weighted_mean" title="Weighted mean" class="mw-redirect">average</a> score of 79, based on 38 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-Metacritic_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metacritic-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Among the major trade journals, Todd McCarthy of <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> called the film an "expansively entertaining special effects extravaganza" with "fresh energy and stylistic polish",<sup id="cite_ref-McCarthy_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCarthy-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> while Kirk Honeycutt of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> praised the film, while nonetheless finding "disappointment [in] a climatic [sic] battle between different Iron Man prototypes [...] how did Tony's nemesis learn how to use the suit?"<sup id="cite_ref-Honeycutt_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Honeycutt-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> In one of the first major-daily newspaper reviews, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lovece" title="Frank Lovece">Frank Lovece</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Newsday" title="Newsday">Newsday</a></i> lauded the film's "emotional truth [...] pitch-perfect casting and plausibly rendered super-science" that made it "faithful to the source material while updating it – and recognizing what's made that material so enduring isn't just the high-tech cool of a man in a metal suit, but the human condition that got him there".<sup id="cite_ref-Lovece_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lovece-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A._O._Scott" title="A. O. Scott">A. O. Scott</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> called the film "an unusually good superhero picture. Or at least – since it certainly has its problems – a superhero movie that's good in unusual ways."<sup id="cite_ref-Scott_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scott-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> Among the specialty press, Garth Franklin of <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Horizons" title="Dark Horizons">Dark Horizons</a></i> commended the "impressive sets and mechanics that combine smoothly with relatively seamless CG", and said, "Robert Downey, Jr., along with director Jon Favreau [...] help this rise above formula. The result is something that, whilst hardly original or groundbreaking, is nevertheless refreshing in its earnestness to avoid dark dramatic stylings in favor of an easy-going, crowd-pleasing action movie with a sprinkle of anti-war and redemption themes".<sup id="cite_ref-Franklin_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Franklin-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Among major metropolitan weeklies, <a href="/wiki/David_Edelstein" title="David Edelstein">David Edelstein</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> magazine called the film "a shapely piece of mythmaking [...] Favreau doesn't go in for stylized comic-book frames, at least in the first half. He gets real with it – you'd think you were watching a military thriller",<sup id="cite_ref-Edelstein_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edelstein-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> while conversely, <a href="/wiki/David_Denby_(film_critic)" title="David Denby (film critic)" class="mw-redirect">David Denby</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> put forth a negative review, claiming "a slightly depressed, going-through-the-motions feel to the entire show [...] <a href="/wiki/Gwyneth_Paltrow" title="Gwyneth Paltrow">Gwyneth Paltrow</a>, widening her eyes and palpitating, can't do much with an antique role as Stark's <a href="/wiki/Girl_Friday_(idiom)" title="Girl Friday (idiom)" class="mw-redirect">girl Friday</a>, who loves him but can't say so; <a href="/wiki/Terrence_Howard" title="Terrence Howard">Terrence Howard</a>, playing a military man who chases around after Stark, looks dispirited and taken for granted".<sup id="cite_ref-Denby_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denby-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a></i><span style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Todd Gilchrist recognized Downey as "the best thing" in a film that "functions on autopilot, providing requisite story developments and character details to fill in this default 'origin story' while the actors successfully breathe life into their otherwise conventional roles".<sup id="cite_ref-Gilchrist_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gilchrist-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> Looking at the sociocultural aspects of the film, Cristobal Giraldez Catalan at <i><a href="/wiki/Bright_Lights_Film_Journal" title="Bright Lights Film Journal">Bright Lights Film Journal</a></i> argues that, "<i>Iron Man</i> is far more than playboy fantasy; it is American foreign policy realized without context....<i>Iron Man</i>, with narrative and directorial precision, once again provides the high-fidelity misogyny and anti-Muslim rhetoric Hollywood is known for."<sup id="cite_ref-Catalan_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalan-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p><a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Corliss" title="Richard Corliss">Richard Corliss</a> named <i>Iron Man</i> as among their favorite films of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Ebert_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ebert-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Corliss_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corliss-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> It was selected by the <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute" title="American Film Institute">American Film Institute</a> as one of the <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute_Awards_2008" title="American Film Institute Awards 2008">ten best films of the year</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-AFIfav_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFIfav-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> and by <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine as one of <i>The 500 Greatest Movies of All Time</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Empire_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Empire-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Tony Stark was also selected by <i>Empire</i> as one of <i>The 100 Greatest Movie Characters of All Time</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-EmpireTony_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EmpireTony-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> and on their list of the <i>100 Greatest Fictional Characters</i>, Fandomania.com ranked him at number 37.<sup id="cite_ref-Fandomania_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fandomania-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequels"><span id="Sequel"></span><span id="Sequels"></span>Sequels</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iron_Man_2"><i>Iron Man 2</i></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_2" title="Iron Man 2">Iron Man 2</a></div>
<p>The sequel, <i>Iron Man 2</i>, was released in the United States on May 7, 2010 with Jon Favreau and Robert Downey, Jr. returning as director and lead, respectively, with a screenplay by <a href="/wiki/Justin_Theroux" title="Justin Theroux">Justin Theroux</a>. <a href="/wiki/Don_Cheadle" title="Don Cheadle">Don Cheadle</a> replaces <a href="/wiki/Terrence_Howard" title="Terrence Howard">Terrence Howard</a> in the role of Colonel Rhodes, who is also seen as <a href="/wiki/War_Machine" title="War Machine">War Machine</a>. Also starring is <a href="/wiki/Gwyneth_Paltrow" title="Gwyneth Paltrow">Gwyneth Paltrow</a> as Pepper Potts; <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Rourke" title="Mickey Rourke">Mickey Rourke</a> as villain <a href="/wiki/Whiplash_(comics)" title="Whiplash (comics)">Ivan Vanko</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sam_Rockwell" title="Sam Rockwell">Sam Rockwell</a> as <a href="/wiki/Justin_Hammer" title="Justin Hammer">Justin Hammer</a>; <a href="/wiki/Scarlett_Johansson" title="Scarlett Johansson">Scarlett Johansson</a> as S.H.I.E.L.D. agent <a href="/wiki/Black_Widow_(Natalia_Romanova)" title="Black Widow (Natalia Romanova)">Natasha Romanoff</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_L._Jackson" title="Samuel L. Jackson">Samuel L. Jackson</a> as S.H.I.E.L.D. director <a href="/wiki/Nick_Fury" title="Nick Fury">Nick Fury</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iron_Man_3"><i>Iron Man 3</i></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_3" title="Iron Man 3">Iron Man 3</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Studios_(production_company)" title="The Walt Disney Studios (production company)" class="mw-redirect">Disney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Studios" title="Marvel Studios">Marvel Studios</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount Pictures</a> announced a May 3, 2013 release date for <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_3" title="Iron Man 3">Iron Man 3</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-IM3_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IM3-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> Favreau said in December 2010 that he would not direct <i>Iron Man 3</i>, opting to direct <i><a href="/wiki/Magic_Kingdom_(film)" title="Magic Kingdom (film)" class="mw-redirect">Magic Kingdom</a></i>, but reprised his role as <a href="/wiki/Happy_Hogan" title="Happy Hogan">Happy Hogan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IM3Favreau_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IM3Favreau-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shane_Black" title="Shane Black">Shane Black</a> directed <i>Iron Man 3</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Black_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> from a screenplay by <a href="/wiki/Drew_Pearce" title="Drew Pearce">Drew Pearce</a>. Robert Downey, Jr. returned as Tony Stark, as did Gwyneth Paltrow as Pepper Potts and Don Cheadle as Colonel Rhodes, who uses the moniker <a href="/wiki/Iron_Patriot#Iron_Patriot_II" title="Iron Patriot">Iron Patriot</a>. <a href="/wiki/Guy_Pearce" title="Guy Pearce">Guy Pearce</a> starred as <a href="/wiki/Aldrich_Killian" title="Aldrich Killian" class="mw-redirect">Aldrich Killian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ben_Kingsley" title="Ben Kingsley">Ben Kingsley</a> as Trevor Slattery.</p>
